Emphasized Sunnah and Recommended Prayers of the Five Daily Prayers
Rulings with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute on supererogatory prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the number of rak'ahs for each sunnah mu'akkadah and mandatory prayer, identify the hadith proof, and apply the Zahir al-Riwayah rule to resolve the intra-Hanafi dispute on the number after Jumu'ah.

Core Idea
Twelve rak'ahs per day are sunnah mu'akkadah; the proof is the hadith of persistence.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq lays out the emphatic sunnah (sunan mu'akkadah) and recommended (mandub) prayers that accompany the five daily prayers. It also reveals an intra-Hanafi dispute on the number of rak'ahs after Jumu'ah and how the principle of Zahir al-Riwayah settles it. By the end, you will be able to identify which prayers are sunnah mu'akkadah and which are merely mandub, and to navigate the proof structure that underpins these rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Acts and Their Rulings
The passage lists several prayers: after Zuhr, Maghrib, Isha (2 each); before Zuhr and before/after Jumu'ah (4 each). These are sunnah mu'akkadah. The passage also mentions recommended (mandub) prayers: 4 before Asr, 4 before and after Isha, 6 after Maghrib.
Distinguish between sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized) and mandub (merely recommended).
2
Locate the Proof for the Emphasized Sunnah
The author cites the hadith: 'Whoever persists (thabara) on twelve rak'ahs in a day and night, Allah will build for him a house in Paradise.' The twelve rak'ahs correspond to the specified sunan mu'akkadah.
The word 'thabara' (persisted) indicates consistency, which is characteristic of sunnah mu'akkadah.
3
Examine the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Jumu'ah Prayer
Although the text says after Jumu'ah is four, it notes that Abdullah ibn Mas'ud and Abu Yusuf transmitted six. The Zahir al-Riwayah (apparent narration) is four based on a saheeh hadith.
The dispute is resolved by preferring the hadith text over the weaker transmission.
4
Apply the Rule of Zahir al-Riwayah
The text explicitly states 'wa wajh zahir al-riwayah...' meaning the relied-upon position is the four rak'ahs hadith. This illustrates how Hanafi methodology prioritises the most sound transmission.
This is a key methodological principle in Hanafi fiqh: Zahir al-Riwayah overrides other narrations when there is conflict.
5
Understand the Classification of Recommended Prayers
The passage explains that the four before Asr, etc., are not sunnah mu'akkadah due to lack of continuous practice; they are mandub. Muhammad al-Shaybani gave a choice between two and four for some, but four is better.
The degree of adherence distinguishes mu'akkadah from mandub.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الوتر والنوافل وبعد الظهر والمغرب والعشاء ركعتان، وقبل الظهر والجمعة وبعدها أربع، أي فرضه أي بعد فرضه أي قبل فرضه وندب الأربع قبل العصر والعشاء وبعده، والستة بعد المغرب، استحب رکعتان: هكذا، خبر ست ركعات أي قبلها أربع ركعات المبتدأ، وقدم سنة الفجر ; لأنها أقوى السنن، ثم سنة المغرب، ثم التي بعد الظهر، ثم التي بعد العشاء، ثم التي قبل الظهر. (ط) وقبل الظهر إلخ الأصل في السنن المؤكدة في الصلوات الخمس قوله عليه: "من ثابر – أي دام - على اثني عشر ركعة في يوم وليلة بنى الله له بيتاً في الجنة"، وفسر على نحو ما ذكر في المتن غير قوله: "بعد الجمعة"، فإنه مذهب عبد الله بن مسعود، وعن أبي يوسف: أنه يصلي بعد الجمعة ستاً; لما روي أنه عليه صلى ووجه ظاهر الرواية قوله عليها: "من كان مصلياً بعد الجمعة فليصل أربع ركعات". (مستخلص) وندب إلخ: لما روي عن علي أنه عليا كان يصلي قبل العصر أربع ركعات وجعله في "الأصل" حسناً، وخيره محمد بين الأربع والركعتين لاختلاف الآثار، وأما الأربع قبل العشاء فليست بسنة; لعدم المواظبة، فكانت مستحبة; ولهذا خير محمد، والأربع أفضل; لأنه أكثر ثواباً والعشاء نظير الظهر، فإنه يجوز التطوع قبلها وبعدها، أما بعدها فلما روي عن ابن عمر له أنه قال: "من صلى بعد العشاء أربع ركعات كان له كمثلهن من ليلة القدر"، وكذا روي عن عائشة لها. (مستخلص) قبل العصر: أي صلاته، وخير محمد بين الأربع والركعتين. (ط) بعد المغرب واختلف هل الأربع بعد الظهر، والست بعد المغرب سوى المؤكدات أو معها؟ والظاهر الثاني، وهو بالخيار بين أن يؤديها بتسليمة أو تسليمتين في الظهر أو بثلاث في المغرب، ولا مانع من تعيينه السنية في الشفع الأول والمندوبية في غيره
Chapter of Witr and Supererogatory Prayers. After Zuhr, Maghrib, and Isha: two rak'ahs each. Before Zuhr, Jumu'ah, and after it: four rak'ahs. And it is recommended to pray four before Asr, before and after Isha, and six after Maghrib. ... The basis for the emphatic sunnahs in the five prayers is his saying: 'Whoever persists in twelve rak'ahs in a day and night, Allah will build for him a house in Paradise.' It was interpreted similar to what is mentioned in the text except his saying 'after Jumu'ah', for it is the opinion of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, and from Abu Yusuf that he prays six after Jumu'ah, but the apparent narration is his saying: 'Whoever prays after Jumu'ah, let him pray four rak'ahs.'
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute. The author states that after Zuhr, Maghrib, and Isha, the sunnah is two rak'ahs; before Zuhr and Jumu'ah and after Jumu'ah it is four rak'ahs. The phrase 'after Jumu'ah' is specific: according to Abdullah ibn Mas'ud it is six, and Abu Yusuf also transmitted six, but the Zahir al-Riwayah (the relied-upon position) is four based on the hadith. The passage then addresses the recommended prayers: four before Asr, four before and after Isha, six after Maghrib. The proof for the four before Asr is the practice of Ali, and Muhammad al-Shaybani gave a choice between two and four due to conflicting reports. The four before Isha are not sunnah but mustahabb due to lack of continuous practice. The four after Isha are recommended based on a report from Ibn Umar. Regarding the six after Maghrib, the author mentions a difference of opinion whether they are additional to the emphatic sunnah or included; the apparent view is the latter. The worshipper may pray them with one taslim or two for Zuhr, and three for Maghrib. The passage also prioritizes the sunnah of Fajr as the strongest, then Maghrib, then after Zuhr, then after Isha, then before Zuhr.

Key Terms
سنن مؤكدة (sunan mu'akkadah): Emphasized sunnah prayers that the Prophet consistently performed and encouraged, leaving only rarely.
مندوب (mandub): Recommended but not emphasized; performing it brings reward but there is no sin in leaving it.
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The most authoritative transmission in the Hanafi school, from the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
ثابر (thabara): To persist or consistently perform; the key word in the hadith indicating the sunnah mu'akkadah nature.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Zahir al-Riwayah, how many rak'ahs should be prayed after Jumu'ah?
A) Two
B) Four
C) Six
D) Eight

Key Takeaway
The twelve rak'ahs of sunnah mu'akkadah are proven by the hadith of persistence, and the Hanafi mufta bihi for after Jumu'ah is four rak'ahs based on Zahir al-Riwayah.

Salah — Prayer

Recommended Prayers: Duha, Istikharah, Tahajjud, and Others
Enumeration of recommended prayers with key rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the recommended prayers mentioned in the text, state their minimum rak'ahs and times, and explain the Hanafi rule that Tahiyyat al-Masjid is fulfilled by any prayer upon entry.

Core Idea
Recommended prayers multiply reward; Tahiyyat al-Masjid is satisfied by any prayer upon entry.

This lesson covers a concise enumeration of recommended (mustahabb) prayers from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. You will learn the key rulings for each: minimum rak'ahs, preferred times, and the important Hanafi rule that Tahiyyat al-Masjid does not require a specific intention — any prayer performed upon entering the mosque suffices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended prayers
Read the passage and list all the prayers mentioned: Duha, Istikharah, Tahajjud, reviving specific nights, two rak'ahs after wudu, travel prayer, Tasbih, and Tahiyyat al-Masjid.
Focus on names only first.
2
Extract minimum rak'ahs and times
For each prayer, note the minimum number of rak'ahs and the preferred time as stated in the text. For example, Duha has a minimum of two rak'ahs and its time is from sunrise to noon, best after a quarter of the day.
Some prayers (like reviving nights) do not specify rak'ahs; note that instead.
3
Understand the Tahiyyat al-Masjid substitution rule
The passage states that performing any obligatory or sunnah prayer upon entering the mosque suffices for Tahiyyat al-Masjid, even without intending it. This is a unique Hanafi ruling.
Also note the exception: it is disliked in makruh times.
4
Memorize the list with key points
Create a mental or written summary: Duha (2+ rak'ahs, after sunrise), Istikharah (2 rak'ahs + du'a), Tahajjud (best after fard), reviving nights (10 Ramadan, Eids, etc.), after wudu (2 rak'ahs before drying), travel (2 rak'ahs on departure and return), Tasbih (specific format), Tahiyyat (any prayer upon entry).
Use this for quick recall.
5
Apply the rulings in practice
Given a scenario (e.g., entering a mosque at a permissible time), decide whether to pray Tahiyyat al-Masjid or substitute with another prayer. Recognise that any prayer counts.
This reinforces the practical difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن الصلوات المندوبة صلاة الضحى فلها ركعتان وكلما زاد فهو أفضل، ووقتها بعد الطلوع إلى الزوال، والمختار بعد ربع النهار، ومنها صلاة الاستخارة، وكيفية صلاة الاستخارة أن يركع ركعتين ويقول: "اللهم إني أستخيرك بعلمك إلخ" كما جاء في الأحاديث، ومنها صلاة الليل – أي التهجد - حثت السنة الشريفة عليها كثيرا، وأفادت أن لفاعلها أجراً عظيماً كما في صحيح مسلم مرفوعا: "أفضل الصيام بعد رمضان شهر المحرم، وأفضل الصلوات بعد الفريضة صلاة الليل، ومنها إحياء ليالي العشر من رمضان، أي قيامها مستوعبا، ويجوز أن يراد غالبها وإحياء ليلتي العيدين وعشر ذي الحجة وليلة النصف من شعبان ومنها ركعتان بعد الوضوء قبل الجفاف، ومنها ركعتا السفر والقدوم منه، ومنها صلاة التسبيح كما رواه عكرمة عن ابن عباس ها، وقد روي هذا الحديث من طرق كثيرة عن . جماعة من الصحابة وقد صححه جماعة ومنها تحية المسجد، أي تحية رب المسجد; لأن المقصود ههنا التقرب إلى الله لا إلى المسجد لقوله عليها: "إذا دخل أحدكم المسجد فلا يجلس حتى يركع ركعتين"، وقد حكي الإجماع على سنيتها إلا في الأوقات المكروهة فإنها تكره، وأداء الفرض ينوب عنها وكذا السنة، وكل صلاة أداها عند الدخول تنوب عنها بلا نية التحية. (فتح ملخصا)
Among the recommended prayers is Salat al-Duha: it has two rak'ahs and each increase is better, its time is from sunrise to zenith, the chosen time is after a quarter of the day. Among them is Salat al-Istikharah: its manner is to pray two rak'ahs and say 'Allahumma inni astakhiruka bi'ilmika...' as in hadith. Among them is Salat al-Layl (tahajjud): the noble Sunnah greatly encouraged it, and it is reported that its doer has great reward as in Sahih Muslim: 'The best fast after Ramadan is Muharram, and the best prayer after the obligatory is the night prayer.' Among them is reviving the nights of the ten [days] of Ramadan, i.e., standing the most part, and reviving the nights of the two Eids, the ten of Dhul Hijjah, and the night of mid-Sha'ban. Among them is two rak'ahs after wudu before drying. Among them is two rak'ahs of travel and return. Among them is Salat al-Tasbih as reported by Ikrimah from Ibn Abbas. Among them is Tahiyyat al-Masjid, i.e., greeting the Lord of the mosque; because the intent here is drawing near to Allah, not the mosque, due to his saying: 'When one of you enters the mosque, let him not sit until he prays two rak'ahs.' Consensus has been reported on its sunniyyah except in disliked times, in which it is disliked. Performing the obligatory prayer [at that time] suffices for it, as does the sunnah. And any prayer one performs upon entry suffices for it without the intention of tahiyyah.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage enumerates several recommended (mustahabb) prayers. It begins with Salat al-Duha (forenoon prayer): minimum two rak'ahs, more is better; time from sunrise to zawal, best after a quarter of the day. Then Salat al-Istikharah: a two-rak'ah prayer followed by a specific supplication for seeking guidance. Then Salat al-Layl (tahajjud): highly meritorious, with a hadith stating it is the best prayer after obligatory. Then the revival of specific nights: the last ten of Ramadan, Eid nights, the ten of Dhul Hijjah, and the night of mid-Sha'ban. Then two rak'ahs after wudu before the limbs dry, and two rak'ahs for travel and arrival. Then Salat al-Tasbih, transmitted from Ibn Abbas via multiple chains. Finally, Tahiyyat al-Masjid: two rak'ahs upon entering the mosque, which is sunnah by consensus except in disliked times. The obligatory prayer or any sunnah prayer performed upon entry suffices for tahiyyah, even without specific intention.

Key Terms
صلاة الضحى (Salat al-Duha): A recommended prayer performed after sunrise until noon, minimum two rak'ahs.
صلاة الاستخارة (Salat al-Istikharah): A two-rak'ah prayer for seeking divine guidance in a matter, followed by a specific du'a.
تحية المسجد (Tahiyyat al-Masjid): Two rak'ahs upon entering the mosque, intended as greeting to Allah.
صلاة التهجد (Salat al-Tahajjud): Night prayer after waking from sleep, highly recommended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum number of rak'ahs for Salat al-Duha?
A) Four
B) Two
C) Six
D) Eight

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that any prayer performed upon entering the mosque suffices for Tahiyyat al-Masjid, without needing specific intention.

Congregational Nafl: Ruling and Exceptions
Ruling on congregational nafl and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on performing nafl in congregation and identify the exceptions (Tarawih and Salat al-Ragha'ib).

Core Idea
Congregational nafl is disliked except Tarawih; Salat al-Ragha'ib in congregation is also disliked.

The Hanafi school generally discourages performing supererogatory prayers in congregation, deeming it makruh. However, there are specific exceptions established by the Sunnah. This lesson clarifies these rulings as presented in the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
Find the phrase stating the general ruling on nafl in congregation.
The text begins with 'يكره النفل بجماعة'.
2
Note the exception
Look for the word 'إلا' which introduces the exception of Tarawih.
Tarawih is exempted because it is a confirmed sunnah performed in congregation.
3
Recognize the specific case
Identify the next sentence about Salat al-Ragha'ib.
This prayer on the first Friday of Rajab is also included in the dislike.
4
Understand the legal classification
Determine that the ruling is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) except for the specified exceptions.
The absence of a stronger prohibition suggests it is not haram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تتمة يكره النفل بجماعة إلا التراويح، وكذا الجماعة في أول جمعة من رجب وهي المسماة بصلاة الرغائب، ولا بأس بأن يقرأ بين الفريضة والسنة الأوراد والتكلم بين السنة والفرض لا يسقطها ولكن ينقص ثوابها، وقيل: يسقط .
Supplement: It is disliked to perform nafl in congregation except tarawih. Similarly, congregation on the first Friday of Rajab, which is called Salat al-Ragha'ib. There is no harm in reciting awrad between the obligatory prayer and the sunnah. Speaking between the sunnah and the obligatory does not nullify it but decreases its reward. It is said: it nullifies.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This 'tatimma' (supplement) lists exceptions to the general permissibility of voluntary prayers. It states that it is makruh (disliked) to pray nafl in congregation, with the exception of Tarawih in Ramadan. It also specifically mentions the prayer known as Salat al-Ragha'ib (the first Friday of Rajab) as being similarly disliked in congregation. The passage then addresses the interval between the fard and sunnah prayers: it is permissible to recite awrad (litanies) between them. As for talking between the sunnah and fard, the stronger opinion is that it does not invalidate the sunnah but reduces its reward; there is a differing view that it does invalidate.

Key Terms
صلاة الرغائب (Salat al-Ragha'ib): A specific prayer performed in congregation on the first Friday of Rajab; the text indicates it is disliked.
أوراد (awrad): Litanies or devotional recitations.
تكلم (takallum): Speaking, specifically between the sunnah and fard prayers in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is allowed without exception
B) It is disliked except Tarawih
C) It is forbidden
D) It is recommended

Key Takeaway
Congregational nafl is disliked (makruh) except for Tarawih; Salat al-Ragha'ib is also disliked.

Actions Between Fard and Sunnah: Recitation and Speech
Rulings on actions between fard and sunnah prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling on reciting awrad and speaking between the fard and sunnah prayers, and differentiate the strong and weak opinions on speech.

Core Idea
Reciting awrad between fard and sunnah is permissible; speaking reduces reward but does not invalidate the sunnah.

The interval between the obligatory prayer and its associated sunnah is a time for devotional recitation. However, speaking during this interval has a nuanced ruling: it does not nullify the sunnah but lessens its spiritual reward. This lesson examines the textual evidence and the difference of opinion within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two actions
Read the passage and note the two distinct actions mentioned between fard and sunnah: reciting awrad and speaking.
The text treats them separately with different rulings.
2
Determine the ruling of awrad
Find the phrase 'لا بأس' which indicates permissibility.
There is no dislike for reciting litanies between fard and sunnah.
3
Analyze the ruling of speaking
Look for the two opinions: the primary view ('لا يسقطها') and the secondary view ('قيل: يسقط').
The primary view is that speaking does not invalidate; the secondary says it does.
4
Understand the legal effect
Note that even if speaking does not invalidate, it still decreases the reward of the sunnah prayer.
Thus it is makruh tanzihi (mildly disliked) to speak, but the prayer remains valid.

Source Text

تتمة يكره النفل بجماعة إلا التراويح، وكذا الجماعة في أول جمعة من رجب وهي المسماة بصلاة الرغائب، ولا بأس بأن يقرأ بين الفريضة والسنة الأوراد والتكلم بين السنة والفرض لا يسقطها ولكن ينقص ثوابها، وقيل: يسقط .

There is no harm in reciting awrad between the obligatory prayer and the sunnah. Speaking between the sunnah and the obligatory does not nullify it but decreases its reward. It is said: it nullifies.

Commentary
This 'tatimma' (supplement) lists exceptions to the general permissibility of voluntary prayers. It states that it is makruh (disliked) to pray nafl in congregation, with the exception of Tarawih in Ramadan. It also specifically mentions the prayer known as Salat al-Ragha'ib (the first Friday of Rajab) as being similarly disliked in congregation. The passage then addresses the interval between the fard and sunnah prayers: it is permissible to recite awrad (litanies) between them. As for talking between the sunnah and fard, the stronger opinion is that it does not invalidate the sunnah but reduces its reward; there is a differing view that it does invalidate.

Key Terms

أوراد (awrad): Litanies or devotional recitations.

Best Manner of Night and Day Nafl: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Ruling on maximum rak'ahs per taslim and intra-Hanafi dispute on optimal mode

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the maximum rak'ahs per taslim and explain the intra-school dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the best mode for night nafl.

Core Idea
Night nafl is best prayed two-by-two (mufta bihi), but four with one taslim is also valid.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses the optimal form of nafl prayers. While it is disliked to exceed four rak'ahs per taslim in the day and eight at night, a deeper dispute exists among the Hanafi imams about whether four with one taslim or pairs is superior. Understanding this ikhtilaf clarifies the range of valid practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on maximum rak'ahs
Start by noting the baseline ruling: it is makruh (disliked) to pray more than four rak'ahs with one taslim in day nafl, and more than eight at night. This sets the outer limit.
The dislike is tanzihi (slight), not tahrimi.
2
Compare Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that four rak'ahs with one taslim is preferable both day and night. His evidence: the Prophet's practice of praying four after Isha and four in Duha, and the principle that a single tahrimah (opening takbir) entails greater merit.
He views the hadith 'Salat al-layl muthna' as referring to the basic form, not the best.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's view
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) argue that night nafl should be prayed in pairs (two rak'ahs per taslim), based on the explicit hadith 'Salat al-layl muthna' and analogy with Tarawih. For day nafl, they agree with Abu Hanifa that four is best.
They prioritize the explicit command over the observed practice.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
According to al-Mi'raj, the fatwa is given according to the Sahibayn's position for night nafl. Thus the operative ruling is to pray night nafl two-by-two.
This is the position of later Hanafi authorities.
5
Note the ancillary ruling on qiyam vs. sujud
The passage concludes that long standing (qiyam) is better than many prostrations, because recitation (qira'ah) is superior to tasbih. This is a separate fiqh principle.
Based on the hadith 'The best prayer is long standing' (qunut).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ف ك وكره الزيادة على أربع بتسليمة في نفل النهار، وعلى ثمان ليلاً، والأفضل فيهما س م ركعات واحدة وكره الزيادة طف زر الليل والنهار رباع، وطول القيام أحب من كثرة السجود والقراءة فرض في ركعتي الفرض في الصلاة وكل النفل والوتر، ولزم النفل بالشروع ولو عند الغروب ركعات فيه قصدا كان الشروع غروب الشمس = وكذا كل عمل ينافي التحريمة على الأصح، والأفضل في النفل غير التراويح الْمَنْزِلُ، إلا لخوف شغل عنها.(فتح) الزيادة على أربع لأن النبي عليه لم يزد على ذلك، أي على أربعة نهاراً وعلى ثمان ليلاً، ولولا الكراهة لزاد على ذلك تعليماً للجواز، فالنفل ليلاً ونهاراً أربع أولى، وقالا بالليالي شفع أفضل، وفي النهار يصلي أربعاً بتسليمة واحدة، وعند الشافعي: الأفضل فيهما مثنى مثنى، ولهما: الاعتبار في الليل بالتراويح، وفي النهار بسنة الظهر، ولما ورد: "صلاة الليل مثنى"، ولأبي حنيفة: "أن النبي عليه كان يصلي بعد العشاء أربعاً"، رواه عائشة، وكان يواظب على أربع في الضحى; ولأنه أدوم تحريمة فيكون الأربع أكثر مشقة وأزيد فضيلة، والتراويح يؤدي بجماعة فيراعى فيها جهة التيسير، وفي "المعراج": أنه بقولهما يفتى اتباعاً للحديث (مستخلص، فتح ثمان ليلاً: أي في نفل الليل; لأنه عليه لم يزد عليه بتسليمة، وقالا : لا يزيد على ركعتين. (ع) كثرة السجود : لقوله عليه: "أفضل الصلاة طول القنوت"، أي القيام وبطول القيام تكثر القراءة، وبكثرة السجود التسبيح، والقراءة أفضل منه.
And it is disliked to increase beyond four with one taslim in day nafl, and beyond eight at night. The best in both is [unclear] one rak'ah. And it is disliked to increase, [unclear] the night and day are four. And long standing is more beloved than many prostrations. ... The increase beyond four is because the Prophet did not increase beyond that, i.e., four during day and eight at night. If not for dislike, he would have increased to teach permissibility. So nafl by night and day: four is preferable. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say: at night, pairs (shaf') is better, and during day one prays four with one taslim. ... For Abu Hanifa: the Prophet used to pray four after Isha, narrated by Aisha, and he continued with four in Duha. ... In al-Mi'raj: fatwa is given according to the two (Sahibayn) following the hadith. ... Many prostrations: because of his saying: 'The best prayer is long standing (qunut)', i.e., standing; with long standing, recitation increases; with many prostrations, tasbih increases; and recitation is better than tasbih.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage addresses the number of rak'ahs in nafl prayers and an intra-Hanafi dispute. The ruling: it is makruh to exceed four rak'ahs with one taslim in day nafl and eight at night. The best mode is debated. Abu Hanifa holds that four is preferable both day and night because the Prophet did not exceed four in day and eight at night, and if it were not disliked, he would have increased to show permissibility. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) say at night, praying in pairs (two rak'ahs) is better, based on the hadith 'Salat al-layl muthna'. For day, they agree with four with one taslim, analogous to the sunnah of Zuhr. The Shafi'i school holds that both day and night are best as two-by-two. The text notes that in al-Mi'raj, fatwa is given according to the Sahibayn, following the hadith. It also mentions that long standing (qiyam) is better than many prostrations, because recitation (qira'ah) is superior to tasbih. The pearl: 'The best prayer is long standing' indicates the virtue of lengthy qiyam.

Key Terms
كراهة (karahah): Disliked (makruh), less severe than haram but still discouraged.
تحريمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that commences prayer and establishes its sacredness.
شفع (shaf'): A pair (two rak'ahs), as opposed to 'witr' (odd).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Four rak'ahs with one taslim
B) Two rak'ahs with one taslim (as a single unit)
C) Two rak'ahs with one taslim, repeated (two-by-two)
D) Eight rak'ahs with one taslim

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi for night nafl is to pray two-by-two, following the Sahibayn's interpretation of the hadith 'Salat al-layl muthna'.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Qira'ah in Fard, Nafl, and Witr: The Hanafi Position and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Ruling on recitation in prayer with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on which rak'ahs require obligatory recitation (qira'ah) in fard, nafl, and witr prayers, and explain the key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i views using the evidence presented.

Core Idea
Recitation is fard in two rak'ahs of fard, every rak'ah of nafl; the last rak'ahs of fard do not require recitation.

Prayer requires recitation of the Quran, but how many rak'ahs must include it as an obligatory element? This seemingly simple question has been debated among the schools. The Hanafi school holds that recitation is fard (obligatory) only in two rak'ahs of any fard prayer, while other schools like the Shafi'i require it in every rak'ah. In this lesson, we will dissect the Hanafi position, the proofs used, and how it responds to the differences with other madhahib, especially regarding nafl and witr prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute and the Hanafi ruling
Start by understanding the core question: How many rak'ahs require fard recitation in a fard prayer? The Hanafi school says two rak'ahs (the first two in a 3 or 4 rak'ah prayer, both in a 2-rak'ah prayer), while other schools differ. Read the opening sentence: 'Wal-qira'atu fardun fi rak'atayhi mutlaqan'.
2
Examine the Hanafi proofs
The Hanafi view is based on the Quranic verse (Al-Muzzammil 73:20): 'So recite what is easy of the Quran.' The imperative indicates obligation, but it does not demand repetition. Additionally, an athar from Ali and Ibn Mas'ud instructs: 'Recite in the first two, and glorify in the last two.' Identify these proofs in the text.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i evidence
The Shafi'i school cites the hadith: 'No prayer except with recitation, and every rak'ah is a prayer.' The Hanafi response interprets this as applying to the two obligatory rak'ahs, not to each individual rak'ah. The phrase 'every rak'ah is a prayer' is not textual for fard recitation.
4
Apply the ruling to nafl and witr
The passage clarifies that for nafl prayers, recitation is fard in every rak'ah because each pair (shaf') is an independent prayer. For witr, it is also fard in every rak'ah as a precautionary measure due to differing views on its status.
5
Understand the Hanafi distinction between fard and wajib
Note that although recitation is fard in two rak'ahs, specifying the first two for that recitation is wajib (necessary). This distinction affects compensation: omitting the fard invalidates the prayer, but omitting the wajib (like reciting in the first two instead of the last two) requires sajdah sahw but does not nullify the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[رمز الحقائق: ٧٩/١] والقراءة فرض: أي في ركعتيه مطلقاً سواء كان ثنائياً أو ثلاثياً أو رباعياً، لكن تعيينها في الأوليين واجب، وقال الشافعي: في كل ركعات فرض؛ لقوله علي: "لا صلاة إلا بقراءة وكل ركعة صلاة، وقال مالك: في ثلاث ركعات؛ إقامة للأكثر مقام الكل تيسيراً، وقال زفر والحسن البصري: في ركعة واحدة؛ لأن الأمر لا يقتضي التكرار، وقال أبو بكر الأصم القراءة ليس بفرض بل هي سنة كسائر الأذكار ; لأن مبنى الصلاة على الأفعال دون الأقوال، والعاجز عن الأفعال كلها القادر على الأقوال لا يخاطب بالصلاة بخلاف العكس، ولنا قوله تعالى: فَاقْرَأُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ (المزمل:۲۰) والأمر بالفعل لا يقتضي التكرار، وإنما أوجبنا في الثانية استدلالا بالأولى; ولأنهما متشاكلان من كل وجه والشفع الثاني يتفارق من الأول في حق السقوط، فلا يلحق به، وروي عن علي ه وابن مسعود له: "اقرأ في الأوليين، وسبح في الأخريين".(عيني، مستخلص) وكل النفل والوتر أفرد الوتر بالذكر; لأنه في الأصح واجب وليس بفرض ولا بنفل، والقراءة فرض في كل ركعات النفل; لأن كل شفع من النفل صلاة على حدة، والقيام إلى الثالثة كتحريمة مبتدأة; ولهذا لا يجب بالتحريمة الأولى إلا ركعتان في الأظهر; ولهذا قالوا: يستفتح في الثالثة، أما كون القراءة فرضا في كل ركعات الوتر فللاحتياط; لأنه شبهة في كون الوتر سنة ثابتة لاختلاف الأحاديث. (مستخلص، فتح)
[Ramz al-Haqaiq: 1/79] And recitation is fard: i.e., in its two rak'ahs absolutely, whether [the prayer] is two, three, or four rak'ahs, but its specification to the first two is wajib. Al-Shafi'i said: in every rak'ah it is fard, due to his saying: 'No prayer except with recitation, and every rak'ah is a prayer.' Malik said: in three rak'ahs, establishing the majority in place of the whole for ease. Zufar and Hasan al-Basri said: in one rak'ah, because the command does not necessitate repetition. Abu Bakr al-Asamm said: recitation is not fard but is sunnah like other dhikr, because the foundation of prayer is actions, not words. Our proof is the verse: 'So recite what is easy of the Quran.' ... And it is related from Ali and Ibn Mas'ud: 'Recite in the first two, and glorify in the last two.' And all nafl and witr. Witr is specifically mentioned because according to the soundest view it is wajib, not fard or nafl. Recitation is fard in every rak'ah of nafl because each pair of nafl is a separate prayer. Standing for the third rak'ah is like a new tahrimah. ... As for the fact that recitation is fard in every rak'ah of witr, it is for precaution, because there is uncertainty about witr being a firmly established sunnah due to differing hadiths.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with inter-madhhab dispute on the obligation of recitation (qira'ah) in prayer. The Hanafi position: recitation is fard (obligatory) in two rak'ahs of every fard prayer, regardless of whether the prayer is two, three, or four rak'ahs. It is wajib (necessary) to recite in the first two rak'ahs specifically. Other views: Shafi'i says it is fard in every rak'ah; Malik says in three; Zufar and Hasan al-Basri say in one; Abu Bakr al-Asamm says it is sunnah only. The Hanafi proof is primarily the Quranic verse 'faqra'u ma tayassara min al-Qur'an' (So recite what is easy of the Quran). The command (amr) indicates obligation but does not necessitate repetition (تكرار). The obligation in the second rak'ah is derived by analogy (istidlal) with the first, because both rak'ahs are similar, but the latter pair differs in that it can be dropped (in case of forgetfulness or travel). An athar from Ali and Ibn Mas'ud supports reciting in the first two and glorifying in the last two. For nafl prayers, recitation is fard in every rak'ah because each pair (shaf') is an independent prayer. For witr, recitation is also fard in every rak'ah as a precautionary measure, since witr is a matter of ikhtilaf (some consider it sunnah, others wajib).

Key Terms
قراءة (qira'ah): Recitation of Quran in prayer; its obligation is disputed among schools.
فرض (fard): Obligatory; omission invalidates the act.
شفع (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs; each pair in nafl is a separate prayer unit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many rak'ahs in a four-rak'ah fard prayer require obligatory recitation according to the Hanafi school?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school stands on the principle that the command to recite does not require repetition, thus recitation is fard in only two rak'ahs of fard prayer, but in every rak'ah of nafl and witr due to their separate structures.

Luzum of Nafl Upon Commencement: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Ruling with inter-madhhab dispute on binding nature of nafl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the binding nature of nafl upon commencement and explain the Shafi'i counter-argument using the Quranic verse from Surah al-Tawbah.

Core Idea
A voluntary act once begun becomes binding in Hanafi; Shafi'i says it remains voluntary.

This lesson examines a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding supererogatory acts of worship. The passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq states the Hanafi position that a nafl becomes binding (lazim) once commenced, whether it is prayer or fasting. It then presents the Shafi'i objection based on the Quranic verse 'There is no way against the doers of good.' Understanding this dispute clarifies how each school views the nature of voluntary worship and the legal consequences of invalidating a commenced nafl.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling given in the text: 'wa lazima al-nafl bi al-shuru'' – the nafl becomes binding by commencement. Note that this applies to both prayer and fasting.
The Hanafi position is presented as the default ruling.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The text explicitly mentions 'al-Shafi'i' and states his view: 'la yalzimahu' – it does not bind him, because he is a volunteer.
The Shafi'i position is that a volunteer (mutabarri') is not bound.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i cites the Quranic verse from Surah al-Tawbah (9:91): 'There is no way against the doers of good.' This is the evidence they use to argue that volunteers are not liable.
The verse is quoted in the text.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Although the text does not detail the Hanafi response here, the Hanafi school interprets the verse as referring to blame for not doing more, not as negating the obligation that arises from commencement. They analogize starting a nafl to making a vow (nadhr), which becomes binding.
The Hanafi response relies on the principle that a voluntary act, once initiated, takes on the rule of a vow.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is clear: if one invalidates a nafl prayer or fast, the Hanafi school requires qada' (making it up), while the Shafi'i school does not require qada'.
This difference directly affects a Muslim's practice when a nafl is invalidated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولزم النفل بالشروع [سواء كان صلاةً أو صوماً. (ط)] وقال الشافعي: لا يلزمه; لأنه متبرع ولا لزوم على المتبرع، قال الله تعالى: ﴿مَا عَلَى الْمُحْسِنِينَ مِنْ سَبِيل (التوبة: ٩١). فمن شرع في النفل ثم أفسده لا يلزمه القضاء، =
And the nafl becomes binding by commencement, whether it is prayer or fasting. Al-Shafi'i said: It does not bind him, because he is a volunteer and there is no binding on a volunteer. Allah said: 'There is no way [of blame] against the doers of good.' So whoever starts a nafl and then destroys it, its qada' is not required.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with an inter-madhhab dispute on whether commencing a supererogatory act (nafl) makes it binding. The Hanafi position: yes, once you begin a nafl (whether prayer or fast), it becomes necessary (lazim) to complete it. If you invalidate it, you must make it up (qada'). The Shafi'i position: no, because a volunteer is not bound; they cite the Quranic verse 'there is no way against the doers of good'. The Hanafi argument is practical: starting the act brings it into the realm of obligation; this is based on the principle that a vow (nadhr) becomes binding, and commencement is analogous. The text also notes the exception: if one cannot complete due to valid reason (illness, etc.), there may be leniency, but the default is binding.

Key Terms
لزوم (luzum): Binding obligation; once an act is commenced, it becomes necessary to complete.
شروع (shuru'): Commencement; the act of beginning a worship.
قضاء (qada'): Making up an act of worship after its prescribed time or after invalidation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) No penalty, it was voluntary.
B) They must perform qada' (make it up).
C) They must give sadaqah.
D) They must repeat the prayer immediately in the same time.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a supererogatory act becomes obligatory once commenced; invalidating it requires making it up (qada').

Preferred Number of Rak'ahs in Nafl Prayers
Dispute on preferred number of rak'ahs in nafl prayers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the number of rak'ahs for nafl prayers by day and night and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
By day, four rak'ahs with one taslim is best; by night, the relied-upon position is to pray in pairs.

In this lesson, we explore a classical intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute regarding the ideal structure of voluntary (nafl) prayers. Imam Abu Hanifa advocated for four consecutive rak'ahs with a single taslim in both day and night, while his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, argued that at night it is better to pray in pairs of two. Later Hanafi authority settles on the opinion of the Sahibayn for night prayers. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to weigh proofs and follow the operative fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Identify what Abu Hanifa holds: that four rak'ahs with one taslim is most virtuous for both day and night, and exceeding four by day or eight by night is disliked (makruh).
This is the zahir al-riwayah position from Imam Muhammad's works.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi opposition (Sahibayn)
Note that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani agree on day but differ at night: they say praying in pairs (two rak'ahs repeatedly) is better at night.
Their analogy is to tarawih and the hadith 'Night prayer is in pairs.'
3
Follow the dalil for each side
Abu Hanifa relies on 'A'isha's report that the Prophet regularly prayed four after 'Isha and four at Duha. The Sahibayn cite the general command 'Night prayer is in pairs' and the practice of tarawih.
Both proofs are from the Sunnah; the dispute is over which analogy is stronger.
4
Examine the Hanafi response to the opposing proof
Abu Hanifa's followers argue that the 'pairs' hadith may refer to obligatory prayers or is abrogated, and that tarawih is a special case due to congregation and ease.
The response does not invalidate the other position, but prefers textual specific reports over analogical extension.
5
Determine the tarjih and mufta bihi
Later Hanafi works (e.g., al-Mi'raj) state that fatwa follows the Sahibayn for night prayers due to the strength of the 'pairs' hadith. For day, the four-rak'ah form remains preferred.
Thus, the operative ruling for a mufti today is: by day, four rak'ahs (or less); by night, pray in twos.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الوتر والنوافل
ف ك وكره الزيادة على أربع بتسليمة في نفل النهار، وعلى ثمان ليلاً، والأفضل فيهما أربع أربع ركعات وكره الزيادة على أربع لأن النبي عليه لم يزد على ذلك، أي على أربعة نهاراً وعلى ثمان ليلاً، ولولا الكراهة لزاد على ذلك تعليماً للجواز، فالنفل ليلاً ونهاراً أربع أولى، وقالا بالليالي شفع أفضل، وفي النهار يصلي أربعاً بتسليمة واحدة، وعند الشافعي: الأفضل فيهما مثنى مثنى، ولهما: الاعتبار في الليل بالتراويح، وفي النهار بسنة الظهر، ولما ورد: "صلاة الليل مثنى"، ولأبي حنيفة: "أن النبي عليه كان يصلي بعد العشاء أربعاً"، رواه عائشة، وكان يواظب على أربع في الضحى؛ ولأنه أدوم تحريمة فيكون الأربع أكثر مشقة وأزيد فضيلة، والتراويح يؤدي بجماعة فيراعى فيها جهة التيسير، وفي "المعراج": أنه بقولهما يفتى اتباعاً للحديث
Chapter of Witr and Nawafil. He said: It is disliked to increase beyond four [rak'ahs] with one taslim in daytime nafl, and beyond eight at night. The best in both is four each. The increase is disliked because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not exceed that; i.e., four by day and eight by night. If it were not disliked, he would have increased to teach permissibility. So nafl by night and day, four is better. The two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] say: by night, pairs are better; by day, one prays four with one taslim. According to al-Shafi'i: the best in both is two by two. Their proof: consideration for night is based on tarawih, and for day on the sunna of Zuhr, and because of the hadith 'Night prayer is in pairs.' For Abu Hanifa: the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to pray four after 'Isha', narrated by 'A'isha, and he persisted on four at Duha; and because four has more continuity of tahrimah, thus more exertion and more virtue. Tarawih is performed in congregation, so ease is considered there. In al-Mi'raj: fatwa is according to the two, following the hadith.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the preferred number of rak'ahs in nafl prayers. The Hanafi school states that it is disliked (makruh) to exceed four rak'ahs with one taslim in daytime nafl and eight at night. The best (afdal) is four rak'ahs day and night with a single taslim. Imam Abu Hanifa supports this by noting that the Prophet never exceeded that number, and would have if it were permitted. Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that at night, praying in pairs (two rak'ahs) is better, based on the practice of tarawih and a hadith 'Night prayer is two by two'. Imam al-Shafi'i also prefers pairs day and night. The commentary weighs these positions, concluding that fatwa follows the Sahibayn due to the hadith evidence, though Abu Hanifa's view has its own proofs. The practical implication: one should pray four rak'ahs with one taslim by day, but eight by night is also valid; however, the more rewarding may be two by two at night according to the later relied-upon position.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): Voluntary, supererogatory prayer beyond the obligatory ones.
شفع (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs (two rak'ahs with one taslim).
تحريمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that one enters the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in this text, what is the best way to pray nafl at night?
A) Four rak'ahs with one taslim
B) Two rak'ahs with one taslim (pairs)
C) Eight rak'ahs with one taslim
D) Any number is equal, no preference

Key Takeaway
By day, pray four rak'ahs with one taslim; by night, pray in pairs—this is the operative Hanafi ruling based on later tarjih.

Preference of Long Standing over Many Prostrations
Comparing virtue of long qiyam versus many sujud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the relative virtue of long standing versus many prostrations and explain the proof from hadith.

Core Idea
Long standing in prayer is better than many prostrations because it increases Quran recitation, which is superior to tasbih.

This passage addresses a common question about prioritising acts within prayer: is it better to lengthen the standing (qiyam) or increase the number of prostrations (sujud)? The Hanafi school answers using a prophetic hadith and a comparative analysis of the acts performed in each posture. Understanding this principle helps one optimise the quality of salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The passage compares two postures in prayer: long standing (qiyam) and many prostrations (sujud). It declares that long standing is more virtuous (afdal).
The ruling is about preference (afdaliyyah), not obligation.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith: 'أفضل الصلاة طول القنوت' (The best of prayer is long standing). This is a saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him).
The hadith is ahad, giving zanni certainty in transmission and meaning.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The term 'qunut' in this context means 'qiyam' (standing), as explained by the author. Lengthening standing increases recitation of the Qur'an, which is more virtuous than the tasbih (glorification) performed in prostration.
The Hanafi school interprets qunut here as standing, not the specific supplication in witr.
4
Derive the practical consequence
In voluntary prayers, one should prioritise lengthening the standing over adding extra prostrations, because recitation is superior to tasbih.
This applies to nafl prayers; obligatory prayers have fixed postures.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كثرة السجود : لقوله عليه: "أفضل الصلاة طول القنوت"، أي القيام وبطول القيام تكثر القراءة، وبكثرة السجود التسبيح، والقراءة أفضل منه.
Many prostrations: because of his (peace be upon him) saying: 'The best of prayer is long standing (qunut)', i.e., standing; with long standing recitation increases, and with many prostrations, tasbih (glorification) increases; and recitation is better than that.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the relative merit of long standing (qiyam) versus many prostrations in prayer. The author states that long standing is superior because it allows more recitation (qira'ah), which is better than the tasbih (glorifications) of prostration. The proof is the hadith: 'The best of prayer is long standing (qunut).' The Hanafi school thus encourages lengthening the standing over performing many supererogatory prostrations, as recitation of Qur'an is more virtuous than tasbih.

Key Terms
قنوت (qunut): The prolonged standing in prayer, specifically the act of reciting Qur'an while standing; not the special supplication (du'a) in witr.
تسبيح (tasbih): Glorification of Allah, such as saying 'Subhanallah' or similar in prostration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is more virtuous in prayer: lengthening the standing or increasing the number of prostrations?
A) Lengthening the standing
B) Increasing prostrations
C) They are equal
D) It depends on the type of prayer

Key Takeaway
Long standing in prayer is more virtuous than many prostrations because it enhances Qur'an recitation, which is superior to tasbih.

Recitation in Prayer: Hanafi Position on Which Rak'ahs
Ruling on where recitation is fard in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on where recitation is fard in fard prayer and explain the reasoning against the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
Recitation is fard in only two rak'ahs of fard prayer; specifying the first two is wajib.

One of the key debates in salah is how many rak'ahs require recitation. The Hanafi school holds that recitation is fard in exactly two rak'ahs, not in every rak'ah as the Shafi'is argue. This lesson unpacks the evidence and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Determine what the dispute is about: in which rak'ahs of fard prayer is recitation (qira'ah) obligatory?
The text lists multiple positions; focus on the Hanafi vs. Shafi'i core.
2
State the Hanafi position
State that recitation is fard in two rak'ahs. For any fard prayer (2, 3, or 4 rak'ahs), it is fard in exactly two. Specifying those two as the first two is wajib.
Wajib means that if one omits recitation in the first two intentionally, the prayer is invalid, but if done unintentionally, sajda al-sahw is required.
3
Identify the opposing school and its proof
Al-Shafi'i holds recitation is fard in every rak'ah of fard prayer, citing the hadiths 'No prayer without recitation' and 'Every rak'ah is a prayer.'
Also note other positions: Malik said three, Zufar said one, Abu Bakr al-Asamm said not fard at all.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response and evidence
The Hanafi response: the Quranic command (73:20) does not imply repetition; the hadiths are general and specified by the practice of the Companions, especially the report from 'Ali and Ibn Mas'ud to recite in the first two and glorify in the last two. Also, the second pair of rak'ahs in a four-rak'ah prayer can be dropped for travelers, showing it is not equivalent.
The Hanafi proof includes Quran, hadith, and qiyas.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
In a four-rak'ah fard, if one omits recitation in the last two, the prayer is valid according to Hanafis (since no fard is missed), but invalid according to Shafi'is.
This matters for fatwa and daily practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقراءة فرض: أي في ركعتيه مطلقاً سواء كان ثنائياً أو ثلاثياً أو رباعياً، لكن تعيينها في الأوليين واجب، وقال الشافعي: في كل ركعات فرض؛ لقوله عليه: "لا صلاة إلا بقراءة" وكل ركعة صلاة، وقال مالك: في ثلاث ركعات؛ إقامة للأكثر مقام الكل تيسيراً، وقال زفر والحسن البصري: في ركعة واحدة؛ لأن الأمر لا يقتضي التكرار، وقال أبو بكر الأصم القراءة ليس بفرض بل هي سنة كسائر الأذكار؛ لأن مبنى الصلاة على الأفعال دون الأقوال، والعاجز عن الأفعال كلها القادر على الأقوال لا يخاطب بالصلاة بخلاف العكس، ولنا قوله تعالى: فَاقْرَأُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ (المزمل:۲۰) والأمر بالفعل لا يقتضي التكرار، وإنما أوجبنا في الثانية استدلالا بالأولى؛ ولأنهما متشاكلان من كل وجه والشفع الثاني يتفارق من الأول في حق السقوط، فلا يلحق به، وروي عن علي وابن مسعود: "اقرأ في الأوليين، وسبح في الأخريين". وكل النفل والوتر أفرد الوتر بالذكر؛ لأنه في الأصح واجب وليس بفرض ولا بنفل، والقراءة فرض في كل ركعات النفل؛ لأن كل شفع من النفل صلاة على حدة، والقيام إلى الثالثة كتحريمة مبتدأة؛ ولهذا لا يجب بالتحريمة الأولى إلا ركعتان في الأظهر؛ ولهذا قالوا: يستفتح في الثالثة. وأما كون القراءة فرضا في كل ركعات الوتر فللاحتياط؛ لأنه شبهة في كون الوتر سنة ثابتة لاختلاف الأحاديث.
And recitation is fard (obligatory): i.e., in its two rak'ahs absolutely, whether the prayer is two, three, or four rak'ahs, but its specification in the first two is wajib. Al-Shafi'i said: fard in every rak'ah of the fard, because of his (peace be upon him) saying: 'No prayer without recitation' and every rak'ah is a prayer. Malik said: in three rak'ahs, establishing the majority in place of the whole for ease. Zufar and al-Hasan al-Basri said: in one rak'ah, because the command does not require repetition. Abu Bakr al-Asamm said: recitation is not fard but sunna like other remembrances, because the foundation of prayer is actions not words, and one who cannot perform any actions but can speak is not addressed to pray, contrary to the opposite. Our proof: Allah's saying: 'So recite what is easy from the Qur'an' (73:20), and the command to an action does not require repetition. We only made it obligatory in the second by inference from the first; because they are similar in every aspect, but the second pair differs from the first in terms of fallibility, so it is not analogized. It is narrated from 'Ali and Ibn Mas'ud: 'Recite in the first two, and glorify in the last two.' And all nafl and witr, witr is mentioned separately because it is wajib according to the sound opinion, not fard nor nafl. Recitation is fard in every rak'ah of nafl because each pair of nafl is a separate prayer, and standing for the third is like a new tahrimah; hence only two rak'ahs are obligated by the first tahrimah in the apparent opinion; and therefore they said: one makes the opening supplication (istiftah) in the third. As for recitation being fard in every rak'ah of witr, it is out of caution because there is ambiguity regarding witr being a confirmed sunna due to differing hadiths.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed inter-madhhab dispute on where recitation (qira'ah) is obligatory in prayer. The Hanafi position: recitation is fard (obligatory) in the two rak'ahs of fard prayer, regardless of whether the prayer is two, three, or four rak'ahs, but specifying which two (the first two) is wajib (obligatory). In nafl and witr, recitation is fard in every rak'ah. The text lists the opinions of other schools and scholars: al-Shafi'i (fard in every rak'ah of fard), Malik (three rak'ahs), Zufar and Hasan al-Basri (one rak'ah), and Abu Bakr al-Asmm (not fard at all). The Hanafi proof is Quran 73:20 ('recite what is easy') and the hadith from 'Ali and Ibn Mas'ud directing recitation in the first two and tasbih in the last two. The reasoning: the second pair of rak'ahs in a four-rak'ah fard is not bound by the same obligation as the first, because it can be dropped (in traveler's prayer). In nafl, each pair is a separate prayer, so recitation is fard in every rak'ah. In witr, it is fard out of precaution due to differing hadith on its status.

Key Terms
فرض (fard): A legally obligatory action based on qat'i evidence; omission invalidates prayer if it is the fard of recitation in two rak'ahs.
تعيين (ta'yin): Specification; here, specifying that the fard recitation occurs in the first two rak'ahs is wajib.
شفع (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs; in four-rak'ah prayers, the first two and last two are each a shaf'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, in a four-rak'ah fard prayer, in how many rak'ahs is recitation fard?
A) All four
B) Two rak'ahs (the first two)
C) Three rak'ahs
D) One rak'ah

Key Takeaway
Recitation is fard in only the first two rak'ahs of any fard prayer; this is based on Quran, hadith, and the practice of the Companions, distinguishing it from the Shafi'i view of every rak'ah.

Nafl Becomes Binding Upon Commencement
Clarifying that voluntary acts become obligatory upon commencement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a commenced nafl prayer or fast becomes binding (lazim) and explain the proof from Quran 47:33, as well as identify the opposing Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
A nafl act becomes wajib upon commencement; you cannot abandon it without compensation.

You may think that voluntary prayers can be abandoned at any time. The Hanafi school teaches otherwise: once you start a nafl, it becomes a binding obligation. This ruling is based on the Quranic command not to invalidate your deeds. In this lesson, we examine the proof and the dispute with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The passage states 'nafl becomes binding upon commencement' for both prayer and fasting. The ruling is that completion is wajib.
2
Locate the Hanafi proof
The author cites Quran 47:33 'Do not invalidate your deeds' as the primary evidence. The reasoning is that the act once started is a good deed that must be preserved.
The proof is dalil naqli.
3
Identify the opposing Shafi'i view
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that a volunteer is not obligated; he cites Quran 9:91 'There is no blame on the good-doers'. For him, one may cancel a nafl without penalty.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
4
Understand the Hanafi response and the two types of obligation
The Hanafi response is that undertaking by action (shuru') creates obligation just as a vow (nadhr) does. The passage also distinguishes two ways nafl becomes binding: by speech (nadhr) or by action (shuru'). Commencement occurs by takbir or by standing to the third rak'ah.
This is an expansion on the basis of obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولزم النفل بالشروع [سواء كان صلاةً أو صوماً. (ط)] وقال الشافعي: لا يلزمه؛ لأنه متبرع ولا لزوم على المتبرع، قال الله تعالى: ﴿مَا عَلَى الْمُحْسِنِينَ مِنْ سَبِيل﴾ (التوبة: ٩١). فمن شرع في النفل ثم أفسده لا يلزمه القضاء، ولنا: أن المؤدى وقع قربة فيلزمه الإتمام صيانة للمؤدى عن البطلان؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلا تُبْطِلُوا أَعْمَالَكُمْ﴾ (محمد:۳۳) تبيين الحقائق: ١/ ٤٣٤] وما يجب على العبد بالتزامه :نوعان :الأول ما يجب بالقول وهو النذر، والثاني: ما يجب بالفعل وهو الشروع، والشروع بأحد الأمرين: إما بالافتتاح أو بالقيام إلى الثالثة؛ لأن القيام إليها بمنزلة تحريمة مبتدأة. وقوله: "عند الغروب والطلوع فيه مراعاة السجع بقوله: "ولزم النفل بالشروع" وإلا لكان تقدم الطلوع على الغروب أولى؛ لأنه مقدم عليه طبعاً كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَسَبِّحْ بِحَمْدِ رَبِّكَ قَبْلَ طُلُوعِ الشَّمْسِ وَقَبْلَ الْغُرُوبِ﴾ (ق:۳۹) (فتح، مستخلص) والطلوع والاستواء، حتى لو أفسده قضاه.(ط)
And nafl becomes binding upon commencement, whether it is prayer or fasting. Al-Shafi'i said: it does not become binding because it is a voluntary act and no obligation arises for a volunteer; Allah says: 'There is no blame on the good-doers' (9:91). So if one starts a nafl then spoils it, he is not obligated to make it up. Our proof: that what is performed is an act of worship, so he must complete it to protect it from invalidation; because of Allah's saying: 'Do not invalidate your deeds' (47:33). What is obligatory upon the servant by his undertaking is two types: (1) what becomes obligatory by speech – that is a vow (nadhr); (2) what becomes obligatory by action – that is commencement (shuru'). Commencement is by one of two ways: either by the opening takbir (iftitah) or by standing to the third rak'ah, because standing to it is like a new tahrimah. And his saying: 'near sunset and sunrise' is for rhythmic balance with his saying 'nafl becomes binding upon commencement'; otherwise, sunrise should have been mentioned before sunset because it naturally precedes, as in Allah's saying: 'And glorify the praises of your Lord before sunrise and before sunset' (50:39). And until even if he spoils it, he makes it up (qada).
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage discusses the binding nature of voluntary worship (nafl). The Hanafi school holds that once a person begins a nafl prayer (or fast), it becomes obligatory (lazim) upon him to complete it. This obligation arises from the act of commencement itself (shuru'), similar to a vow. The proof is the Quranic verse 'Do not invalidate your deeds' (47:33), meaning one must preserve the integrity of the worship he has entered. The commentary distinguishes two ways a nafl can become binding: by speech (nadhr/vow) and by action (shuru'/commencement). Commencement itself occurs by the opening takbir (tahrimah) or, in a four-rak'ah nafl, by standing up for the third rak'ah (which is considered a new tahrimah). The text also addresses the Shafi'i objection that a volunteer is not obligated. The Hanafi response is that the act itself becomes a 'good deed' (qurbah) that must be protected. The mention of 'near sunset and sunrise' clarifies that the ruling applies even at those times, and if one spoils the prayer, he must make it up (qada).

Key Terms
شروع (shuru'): Commencement; the act of initiating a voluntary worship, which makes completion obligatory.
لزوم (luzum): The quality of being binding; a nafl becomes lazim (binding) upon the person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if someone starts a nafl prayer but spoils it before completing?
A) They are not required to make it up
B) They must make it up (qada)
C) It is automatically forgiven
D) They must complete it without qada?

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, once you start a nafl prayer or fast, it becomes wajib to complete it; if you invalidate it, you must make it up.

Obligation to Complete a Voluntary Act Once Started
Ruling with proof: commencement obligates completion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that commencing a nafil renders its completion wajib, identify its proof from Quran and qiyas, and apply it to scenarios of commencement.

Core Idea
Starting a nafil makes it wajib to complete; breaking it requires qada.

Many assume voluntary acts can be abandoned at will. Hanafi fiqh differs: once you begin a nafil prayer, it becomes binding upon you. This lesson unpacks the evidence and logical categories behind this ruling, drawing from Quran and resemblance to vows.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its scope
Identify the act (nafil worship) and the ruling (wajib to complete). Note the two ways commencement occurs: opening takbir or standing for the third rak'ah.
The ruling applies to all nafil acts of worship, with prayer as the primary example.
2
Locate the primary proof
The Quranic verse 'Do not invalidate your deeds' (47:33) is cited. Understand that starting a nafil makes it a valid deed; invalidating it would oppose this prohibition.
The Hanafi usul principle: an imperative (nahy too) indicates obligation unless overridden.
3
Analyze the supporting qiyas
The passage compares obligations from speech (nadhr) and from action (shuru'). Both create binding commitments. Recognise this as qiyas: just as a vow becomes obligatory by speech, commencement makes completion obligatory by action.
This qiyas operates on the shared illa of personal commitment.
4
Examine the ikhtilaf and consequence
Note that the Shafi'i school does not hold this obligation. The passage concludes that if one invalidates the nafil, qada (making it up) is required. This is the mufta bihi position.
The practical difference: if a Shafi'i breaks a nafil, no qada; a Hanafi must make it up.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولنا: أن المؤدى وقع قربة فيلزمه الإتمام صيانة للمؤدى عن البطلان؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلا تُبْطِلُوا أَعْمَالَكُمْ (محمد:۳۳) وما يجب على العبد بالتزامه :نوعان :الأول ما يجب بالقول وهو النذر، والثاني: ما يجب بالفعل وهو الشروع، والشروع بأحد الأمرين: إما بالافتتاح أو بالقيام إلى الثالثة؛ لأن القيام إليها بمنزلة تحريمة مبتدأة. وقوله: "عند الغروب والطلوع فيه مراعاة السجع بقوله: "ولزم النفل بالشروع" وإلا لكان تقدم الطلوع على الغروب أولى؛ لأنه مقدم عليه طبعاً كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَسَبِّحْ بِحَمْدِ رَبِّكَ قَبْلَ طُلُوعِ الشَّمْسِ وَقَبْلَ الْغُرُوبِ (ق:۳۹) والطلوع والاستواء، حتى لو أفسده قضاه.
And for us: that what was performed was an act of worship, so it is necessary for him to complete it, to preserve the performed act from invalidation; due to His statement, the Exalted: {And do not invalidate your deeds} (Muhammad:33). And what is obligatory upon the servant by his commitment is of two types: the first is what becomes obligatory by speech, and that is a vow; and the second is what becomes obligatory by action, and that is commencement. And commencement is by one of two things: either by the opening takbir or by standing up for the third rak'ah; because standing for it is like an initial tahrimah. And his saying: 'At sunset and sunrise it is observing the rhyme of his saying: 'And the supererogatory becomes binding by commencement'' otherwise the priority of sunrise over sunset would be more appropriate; because it is naturally ahead of it, like His statement, the Exalted: {And exalt [Allah] with praise of your Lord before the rising of the sun and before the [sun's] setting} (Qaf:39). And sunrise and its zenith, even if he invalidates it, he makes it up.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The author establishes the Hanafi principle that once a person begins a voluntary act of worship (like a nafil prayer), it becomes obligatory (wajib) to complete it. The proof is the Quranic verse 'Do not invalidate your deeds' (47:33). The author then explains that obligations arising from a person's commitment are of two types: (1) by speech, i.e., a vow (nadhr), and (2) by action, i.e., commencement (shuru'). Commencement occurs either by the opening takbir (tahrimah) or by standing up for the third rak'ah in a four-rak'at nafil prayer, because that standing is like a new tahrimah. The author also mentions that the phrase 'at sunset and sunrise' is merely observing rhyme in the matn, and the actual ruling is that the obligation to complete a nafil starts with commencement. The Quranic verse about glorifying before sunrise and sunset is cited to show natural precedence. The conclusion is that if one invalidates a nafil prayer after starting it, one must make it up (qada). This is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الشروع (al-shuru'): Commencement of an act of worship, which, in the case of nafil, creates an obligation to complete it.
تحريمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir that makes the prayer begin and prohibits otherwise permissible actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the second type of obligation that becomes binding by a person's commitment?
A) The vow (nadhr)
B) Commencement (shuru')
C) Recitation (qira'ah)
D) Intention (niyyah)

Key Takeaway
Commencing a nafil makes its completion wajib; breaking it without valid reason requires qada.

Ruling on Performing Voluntary Prayers While Sitting
Discusses permissibility of nafil while sitting, with intra-Hanafi dispute on building.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sitting during nafil prayers and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding changing from standing to sitting.

Core Idea
It is permissible to pray nafil while sitting; only a takbir obligates the prayer, not standing.

This lesson clarifies the permissibility of performing optional prayers in a seated position, even for someone capable of standing. The passage also addresses a specific intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether one who starts a nafil standing may later sit without excuse. Understanding this distinction deepens appreciation of how obligation works in voluntary worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage opens with the ruling that a responsible person may perform nafil prayers while sitting. Note that this applies to all nafil, including tarawih and the sunnah of Fajr.
The ruling is general, not restricted to those with an excuse.
2
Locate the hadith proof
The hadith 'صلاة القاعد على صلاة القائم إلا من عذر' is cited. Recognize that this is a hadith ahad (zanni al-thubut) but sufficient for a non-obligatory ruling. The hadith implies validity of sitting prayer, albeit with half reward.
The exception (excuse) indicates that even without reward, the prayer is valid; so sitting is allowed even without excuse.
3
Understand the ikhtilaf on building (bina')
The passage discusses 'bina'': if one starts nafil standing, can he sit later without excuse? Abu Hanifa permits; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad do not. Grasp the practical scenario.
This is an intra-Hanafi disagreement, not with another school.
4
Analyze the qiyas and rebuttal
The Sahibayn analogize to a vow (nadhr): just as a vow requires completion exactly as pledged, so starting a prayer creates an obligation to complete it with the same postures. Abu Hanifa rebuts by distinguishing the source of obligation: in nadhr it is the name 'prayer' (which includes standing), in commenced nafil it is only the tahrimah (which does not include standing).
The distinction rests on the nature of the obligation: name vs. act of initiation.
5
Apply to common scenarios
The ruling applies to tarawih and sunnah of Fajr. In practice, one may sit for any nafil from the start, or sit after starting standing if following Abu Hanifa's view (mufta bihi).
If sitting due to excuse, it is permissible by consensus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويتنفل قاعداً:[ أي المكلف حال كونه قاعداً كما في التشهد، وبه يفتى. ] أطلقه فيشمل التراويح؛ إذ الأصح فيها الجواز، وسنة الفجر أيضاً، وقيد بالقاعد؛ لأن تنفل المضطجع بلا عذر غير صحيح لكن له نصف أجر القائم؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: "صلاة القاعد على صلاة القائم إلا من عذر، وقيل: يقعد تربعاً، والصحيح أن يقعد كما في التشهد. وبناء: [يعني مبتدءا وبانيا، أو في وقت الابتداء وحالة البناء، وصورة الابتداء ظاهرة بأن يحرم قاعدا، وصورة البناء وصلى بعدها ثم كملها قاعداً بلا عذر يجوز عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن القيام ليس بركن في النفل، وعندهما: لا يجوز؛ لأنه بالشروع صار ملزماً فأشبه النذر .] خلافاً لهما قياساً على مسألة النذر، فكما أنه لا يخرج عن عهدة ما لزمه بنذر الصلاة إلا بالقيام فكذا ما شرع فيه قائماً. وللإمام أن الوجوب في النذر باسم الصلاة، وهي تصرف إلى الأركان من القيام والقراءة وغيرها، أما الوجوب فيما شرع فبالتحريمة، وهي لا توجب القيام، وإنما قيد بالقادر؛ لأنه لو قعد بعذر جاز اتفاقاً.
And he may perform voluntary prayer while sitting: meaning the responsible person while he is sitting, like in the tashahhud, and by this fatwa is given. It is unrestricted, so it includes tarawih; for the correct view is its permissibility, and also the sunnah of Fajr. And it is restricted to sitting; because the voluntary prayer of the one lying down without an excuse is not valid, but he gets half the reward of the one standing; due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'The prayer of the sitting is half the prayer of the standing, except due to an excuse.' And it is said: he sits cross-legged, and the correct view is that he sits like in the tashahhud. And building: meaning starting and building, or at the time of starting and the state of building. The case of starting is apparent by making the tahrimah while sitting. The case of building is that he prays (some rak'ats) then completes them sitting without an excuse—this is permissible according to Abu Hanifa because standing is not a pillar in nafil. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): it is not permissible because by starting he becomes obligated, so it resembles a vow. Contrary to them by analogy on the issue of vow: just as one does not discharge what became obligatory by a vow of prayer except by standing, so too for what he started standing. And for the Imam (Abu Hanifa), the obligation in a vow is by the name of prayer, which is applied to the pillars of standing, recitation, etc. As for the obligation in what he started, it is by the tahrimah, which does not necessitate standing. It is only restricted to the capable because if he sits due to an excuse, it is permissible by agreement.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement and expansion. It addresses two issues: (1) performing voluntary prayers while sitting, and (2) changing from standing to sitting during a voluntary prayer. The author (commentator) explains the matn's phrase 'and he may perform voluntary prayer while sitting.' This applies even to tarawih and the sunnah of Fajr. The evidence is the hadith that the prayer of one sitting is half that of one standing, except for excused persons. The preferred posture is sitting as in tashahhud (i.e., sitting on the left foot). The second issue is 'building' (bina'): if one starts a nafil prayer standing, may he later sit without an excuse? Abu Hanifa says yes, because standing is not a pillar for nafil; the obligation is by the tahrimah (opening takbir), which does not necessitate standing. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say no, because once started, the prayer becomes obligatory and must be completed as started, analogous to a vow where one must stand if the vow was to pray standing. Abu Hanifa distinguishes between vow (where the obligation is tied to the name 'prayer' which includes standing) and commencement (where the obligation is only by the tahrimah). The passage concludes that if one has an excuse, sitting is permissible by consensus.

Key Terms
بناء (bina'): Building: continuing a prayer started standing by sitting without excuse; a point of ikhtilaf.
تحريمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir; the source of obligation to complete the prayer, but not the source of specific postures.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the prayer becomes wajib only by the takbir, which does not require standing
B) Because the hadith says sitting gives half reward
C) Because nafil is always allowed to be shortened
D) Both A and C

Key Takeaway
In nafil prayers, sitting is permissible even without excuse; starting standing does not obligate remaining standing because the obligation is only by the takbir.

Ruling on Invalidating a Four-Rak'ah Nafl Prayer
Ruling on niyyah and invalidation of four-rak'ah nafl with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute on invalidating a four-rak'ah nafl and apply the rule to determine how many rak'ahs to repeat.

Core Idea
Omitting recitation in the first pair invalidates the takbirat al-ihram, so the second pair never starts — Sahibayn; Abu Yusuf disagrees.

When a four-rak'ah nafl prayer is invalidated, there is a disagreement within the Hanafi school on how many rak'ahs must be repeated. The dispute hinges on whether recitation in the first pair is a condition for the second pair's validity. This lesson examines the reasoning of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and Abu Yusuf, and identifies the mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and key terms
The passage discusses a four-rak'ah nafl prayer that is invalidated, either before or after the first sitting. Key terms: 'tahrimah' (takbirat al-ihram) and 'shaf‘' (pair of rak'ahs).
The invalidation here is due to omitting recitation (qira'ah) in the first pair.
2
Understand the two’s reasoning (Sahibayn)
The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that omitting recitation in the first pair, even in one rak'ah, invalidates the tahrimah. Since the tahrimah is the foundation, the second pair never validly commences. Therefore, only the first pair is corrupted, and two rak'ahs must be repeated.
This is based on the principle that the tahrimah must be valid for the entire prayer.
3
Understand Abu Yusuf’s reasoning
Abu Yusuf argues that recitation in the first pair is not a condition for the validity of the second pair's commencement. Thus, when recitation is omitted, the first pair is corrupted, but the second pair was validly started and then corrupted later. Hence, all four rak'ahs must be repeated.
Abu Yusuf treats the two pairs as independent in this respect.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: according to Sahibayn, repeat two rak'ahs; according to Abu Yusuf, repeat four. The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is that of Sahibayn.
The text's structure and standard practice favor Sahibayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الوتر والنوافل
لو نوى أربعاً وأفسده بعد القعود الأول أو قبله، أو لم يقرأ فيهن شيئاً، أو قرأ في أربع ركعات الأوليين، أو الأخريين أو الأوليين وإحدى الأخريين، أو الأخريين وإحدى الأوليين، لا غير، وأربعاً لو قرأ في إحدى الأوليين أو إحدى الأوليين وإحدى الأخريين لا غير.
- لأن ترك القراءة في الشفع الأول ولو في إحداهما يبطل التحريمة فلا يصح البناء على التحريمة لبطلانها، الثالث: لم يقرأ فيهن شيئاً، فعليه قضاء ركعتين عند الطرفين؛ لأنه صح شروعه، وقد أفسد الشفع الأول بترك القراءة فيه، فلزم عدم صحة الشروع في الثاني، وعند أبي يوسف يقضي أربعاً؛ لأنه لا يشترط لصحة الشروع في الثاني وجود القراءة في الأول، الرابع: قرأ في إحدى الأخريين لا غير، فعليه قضاء ركعتين عندهما، وعند أبي يوسف قضاء الأربع.(فتح)
Chapter of Witr and Supererogatory Prayers: If he intended four (rak'ahs) and invalidated it after the first sitting or before it, or did not recite anything in them, or recited in four rak'ahs: the first two, or the last two, or the first two and one of the last two, or the last two and one of the first two, only, and (he intended) four if he recited in one of the first two or one of the first two and one of the last two only. - Because omitting recitation in the first pair, even in one of them, invalidates the takbirat al-ihram, so building upon the takbirat al-ihram is invalid due to its nullification. Third: he did not recite anything in them; upon him is to repeat two rak'ahs according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), because his commencement was valid, and he corrupted the first pair by omitting recitation in it, so the second is not validly commenced. According to Abu Yusuf, he repeats four, because for the validity of commencing the second, the existence of recitation in the first is not a condition. Fourth: he recited in one of the last two only; upon him is to repeat two rak'ahs according to them, and according to Abu Yusuf, repeating four. (Fath)
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of invalidating a four-rak'ah nafl prayer. The matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents scenarios. The commentary from Fath al-Qadir explains the reasoning. The dispute centers on whether recitation in the first pair is necessary for the second pair to be validly commenced. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say recitation is required, so if omitted, the second pair never started. Abu Yusuf disagrees, saying recitation is not a condition for the second, so the second pair is validly commenced and then corrupted, requiring repetition of four. The relied-upon position is that of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) as indicated by the text's preference.

Key Terms
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The takbirat al-ihram that commences the prayer; its validity is required for the entire prayer.
الشفع (al-shaf‘): A pair of rak'ahs; in a four-rak'ah nafl, the first two rak'ahs form the first pair, the last two form the second.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Four rak'ahs
B) Two rak'ahs
C) One rak'ah
D) None, the prayer is valid

Key Takeaway
In a four-rak'ah nafl, omitting recitation in the first pair invalidates only that pair according to Sahibayn, so two rak'ahs are repeated.
