Making up the Sunnah Before Dhuhr When Joining Congregation
Ruling on qada of sunnah before Dhuhr when joining imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making up the sunnah before Dhuhr when joining the congregation, explain the disagreement between Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, and apply the mufta bihi opinion.

Core Idea
When joining the congregation, make up the missed sunnah before Dhuhr first, then the shaf' — the relied-upon view.

When a person joins the Dhuhr congregation after the imam has started, they may miss the four rak'ahs of sunnah before the fard. How should they make up this missed sunnah and the shaf' (the two rak'ahs after Dhuhr)? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on the order. This lesson unpacks the ruling from the matn and commentary, clarifies the basis of the ikhtilaf, and identifies the mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The scenario is a person who joins the Dhuhr congregation after the imam has started and misses the four rak'ahs of sunnah before Dhuhr.
2
State the matn ruling
The matn says: one makes up the four rak'ahs in its time before the shaf' (sunnah after Dhuhr).
This implies an order: first the missed four, then the shaf'.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf holds the matn's order (four first, then shaf'), while Muhammad holds the opposite (shaf' first, then four). Identify each position.
The text explicitly mentions this disagreement.
4
Understand the basis of disagreement
The disagreement is based on whether the missed sunnah is considered 'nafl mubtada'' (supererogatory, time passed) or 'sunnah' (established practice). Those who consider it nafl give precedence to the shaf'; those who consider it sunnah give precedence to the missed four.
This classification determines the order.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text states 'wa bihi yufta' (and according to him fatwa is given) for Abu Yusuf's view. Thus the relied-upon position is to pray the four first, then the shaf'.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب إدراك الفريضة

قضى التي قبل الظهر في وقته قبل شفعه

قضى التي إلخ: أي إذا شرع مع الإمام وترك الأربع قبل الظهر يقضي في وقته عند الجمهور، كذا روي عن أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه، وإطلاق اسم القضاء على ما ليس بواجب مجاز، ولهذا لا ينوي القضاء فيها، وإنما لم يقض سنة الفجر بعد أداء الفرض لكراهة التنفل بعده بخلاف الظهر، والتقييد بالتي قبل الظهر وكذا قبل الجمعة للاحتراز عن التي قبل العشاء؛ لأنها مندوبة فلا تقضى أصلاً، وكذا التي قبل العصر بل أولى، وكراهة التنفل بعده، وقيل: لا يقضيه، ثم قال أبو يوسف يصلي الأربع أولا ثم شفعه وبه يفتى، وقال محمد بعكسه، وذكر صدر الشهيد الاختلاف على العكس إما تقديم القبلية مع أنه فات محلها على البعدية التي لم يفت محلها، فلا خلاف في ترجيحه، قيل: الاختلاف بناء على أنه نفل مبتدأ أو سنة، فمن قال إنه نفل؛ لأنه ذات محله لا يقدمه عليه، ومن قال: إنه سنة يقدمه عليه، فإن خرج الوقت لم يقضه وحده ولا تبعاً، وكذا سائر السنن، أما عدم قضاء السنن وحدها بعد خروج الوقت فمما لا خلاف فيه إلا سنة الفجر عند محمد، وأما عدم قضائها تبعاً فهو الصحيح.
Chapter of Catching the Obligatory Prayer. He makes up the (sunnah) before dhuhr in its time before its shaf' (i.e., the two rak'ahs of sunnah after dhuhr). He makes up that which was before dhuhr etc.: i.e., when he starts with the imam and leaves the four (rak'ahs) before dhuhr, he makes them up in its time according to the majority. Thus it is narrated from Abu Hanifa and his two companions. Calling it 'qada' for what is not obligatory is metaphorical, hence he does not intend qada in it. The sunnah of Fajr is not made up after performing the fard due to dislike of voluntary prayer after it, unlike Dhuhr. The restriction to that before Dhuhr and similarly before Jumu'ah is to exclude that before Isha, because it is recommended and not made up at all; similarly that before Asr is even more so. It is said: he does not make it up. Then Abu Yusuf said: he prays the four first then its shaf', and according to him fatwa is given. Muhammad said the opposite. Sadr al-Shahid mentioned the difference is reversed: whether to give precedence to the (sunnah) before (the fard) whose time has passed over the (sunnah) after whose time has not passed; there is no dispute about preferring (the former). It is said: the disagreement is based on whether it is a nafl mubtada' or a sunnah. Whoever says it is nafl because its time has passed does not give it precedence; whoever says it is sunnah gives it precedence. If time exits, he does not make it up alone nor as a follow-up, and similarly for other sunan. As for not making up the sunan alone after time exits, there is no disagreement except for the sunnah of Fajr according to Muhammad. And as for not making them up as a follow-up, that is the correct view.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the qada (make-up) of the sunnah prayer before Dhuhr when one joins the congregation. The matn states that one makes up the four rak'ahs of sunnah before Dhuhr in its time, before performing the two rak'ahs of sunnah after Dhuhr (the shaf'). The commentary clarifies that this applies when one starts with the imam and misses those sunnah rak'ahs. The ruling is based on a narration from Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. Notably, the term 'qada' is used metaphorically since the sunnah is not obligatory. The reason the Fajr sunnah is not made up after its fard is due to the dislike of supererogatory prayer after Fajr, whereas Dhuhr has no such restriction. The dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad concerns the order: Abu Yusuf says to pray the missed four first, then the two (shaf'), and this is the relied-upon position; Muhammad says the opposite. The commentary explains that the underlying principle is whether the sunnah before Dhuhr is considered a 'nafl mubtada' (beginning supererogatory) or a 'sunnah' (established practice). Those who call it nafl argue its time has passed and thus should not be given precedence; those who call it sunnah argue it should be prioritized. After the time for Dhuhr expires, these sunnah prayers are not made up at all — neither individually nor as a follow-up to the fard — except for the Fajr sunnah according to Muhammad. This ruling applies to all similar sunan prayers.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada): In this context, 'qada' is used metaphorically for making up a sunnah prayer that was missed; it is not legally required like qada of a fard.
شفع (shaf'): The two rak'ahs of sunnah that are prayed after the fard of Dhuhr (also called sunnah ba'diyah).
نفل مبتدأ (nafl mubtada'): A supererogatory prayer that is not a confirmed sunnah (ghayr mu'akkadah) and is considered optional without emphasis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position, in what order should the missed sunnah before Dhuhr and the shaf' (sunnah after Dhuhr) be prayed when one joins the congregation?
A) Pray the shaf' first, then the four rak'ahs of sunnah before Dhuhr.
B) Pray the four rak'ahs of sunnah before Dhuhr first, then the shaf'.
C) The shaf' is not prayed; only the four rak'ahs are made up.
D) Neither is made up; one simply continues with the fard.

Key Takeaway
The missed sunnah before Dhuhr is made up in its time before the shaf', following the relied-upon view of Abu Yusuf.

Catching One Rak'ah: Oath, Virtue, and Supererogatory Rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between catching the congregation for oath purposes and catching its virtue, and state the ruling on performing sunnah rawatib before the fard when time is tight.

Core Idea
Catching one rak'ah secures virtue but does not fulfill an oath to pray with congregation; rawatib are prayed before fard if time allows.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies a crucial nuance: arriving late and catching even one rak'ah grants the blessing of congregational prayer, but does not legally constitute 'praying with the congregation' for oaths. The second part provides guidance on when a worshipper should perform the confirmed sunnah prayers before the obligatory prayer, emphasizing the priority of the fard if time is tight.

Guided Path
1
Identify the masbuq and the core issue
Recognize that the passage addresses a masbuq (latecomer) who catches one rak'ah behind the imam. The question is whether this fulfills the condition of praying with jama'ah (for oaths) or merely grants its virtue.
Masbuq is different from lahiq; the lahiq is legally behind the imam.
2
Examine the oath example from al-Jami'
Analyze the scenario: A man swears 'My slave is free if I pray Dhuhr with congregation' and then catches only one rak'ah. According to the Hanafi ruling, the oath is not broken because he is not considered to have prayed the entire prayer with the congregation.
This shows that 'praying with congregation' means sharing the entire prayer from the beginning (or at least the majority) with the imam.
3
Contrast with the hadith on catching Asr
The hadith 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Asr before sunset has caught Asr' uses 'catching' for the whole prayer. The Hanafis distinguish: catching the prayer (validity) is different from catching the congregation (for oaths). The hadith applies to validity, not to the definition of congregation.
This distinction avoids contradiction.
4
Understand the virtue of congregation
The passage states that even catching the tashahhud secures the virtue (fadl) of jama'ah, though the reward is less than one who prayed the whole prayer with the imam. This is by consensus.
The rak'ah is not a minimum; even less counts for virtue.
5
Apply the supererogatory ruling
The matn says: 'and he prays supererogatory before the fard if safe from losing time, otherwise not.' The commentary elaborates: if performing the fard with congregation, one definitely prays the rawatib sunan; if alone, one should also pray them unless time is tight. For non-rawatib (additional sunan), there is a choice.
This applies to all rawatib, not just Dhuhr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يصل الظهر بجماعة بإدراك الركعة بل أدرك فضلها، ويتطوّع قبل الفرض إن أمن فوت الوقت وإلا لا

(ط) ولم يصل الظهر إلخ: أي مسبوق أدرك خلف الإمام ركعة فليس مدركاً للجماعة، بخلاف اللاحق؛ لأنه خلف الإمام حكماً، وقوله: "بل أدرك فضلها" لكن ثوابه دون المدرك؛ لفوات التكبيرة الأولى، وليست الركعة قيداً احترازياً عن إدراك ما دونها، بل التقييد اتفاقي؛ لما تحقق أن مدرك التشهد محرز فضل الجماعة بالاتفاق، وأصله ما ذكر في "الجامع": رجل قال: "عبده حر إن صلى الظهر بجماعة"، فأدرك ركعة لم يحنث، والمراد بالركعة مطلقاً سواء كانت رباعية أو ثنائية أو ثلاثية ولو قال عبده حر إن أدرك الظهر حنث بإدراك الركعة؛ لأن إدراك الشيء إدراك آخره، وعلى هذا قوله عليه: "من أدرك ركعة من العصر قبل أن تغرب الشمس فقد أدرك العصر". (فتح)

بجماعة: يعني إذا حلف بأن قال: عبدي حر إن صليت الظهر بجماعة لا يكون مصلياً بجماعة بإدراك ركعة؛ لأنه منفرد ببعضه، فلا يحنث إلا إذا صلى كله أو أكثره بجماعة حنث . (ع)

أدرك فضلها: أي فضل الجماعة، ولو بإدراك التشهد لكن ثوابه دون المدرك. (ط)

وإلا لا [ أي وإن لم يأمن فوت الوقت بأن كان فيه ضيق. (ع)] قيل: هذا في سنة العصر والعشاء دون الفجر والظهر ، قلت هذا يحتاج إلى التفصيل، فنقول: التطوع على وجهين: سنة مؤكدة وهي الرواتب، وغير مؤكدة وهي ما زاد عليها، والمصلي لا يخلو إما أن يكون يؤدي المكتوبة بجماعة أو منفرداً، فإن كان بجماعة يصلي السنن الرواتب قطعاً، ولا يتخير فيها مع الإمكان، وإن كان منفرداً فكذلك في رواية، وقيل: يتخير، والأول أحوط، إلا إذا خاف فوت الوقت، وأما غير الرواتب فإنه يتخير فيها مطلقا. (عيني)
And he did not pray Dhuhr with congregation by catching one rak'ah, but he caught its virtue. And he prays supererogatory before the fard if he is safe from losing the time, otherwise not. (T) 'And he did not pray Dhuhr etc.': i.e., a masbuq who catches one rak'ah behind the imam is not a catcher of the congregation, unlike the lahiq because he is behind the imam legally. And his statement 'but he caught its virtue': but his reward is less than the one who caught (the full congregation) due to missing the first takbir. The rak'ah is not a restrictive condition for catching something less; rather the restriction is coincidental because it is established that one who catches the tashahhud secures the virtue of the congregation by consensus. The basis is what is mentioned in al-Jami': a man said 'My slave is free if he prays Dhuhr with congregation', and he caught one rak'ah, he is not sinning (i.e., the oath is not broken). The intention of rak'ah is absolute, whether four, two, or three. If he said 'My slave is free if he catches Dhuhr', then he would break the oath by catching one rak'ah because catching a thing is catching its end. And upon this is his statement (peace be upon him): 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Asr before the sun sets has caught Asr.' (Fath) 'With congregation': means if he swears saying 'My slave is free if I pray Dhuhr with congregation', he is not considered praying with congregation by catching one rak'ah because he is alone in part of it; thus he does not break the oath unless he prays all or most of it with congregation. (A) 'He caught its virtue': i.e., the virtue of congregation, even by catching the tashahhud, but his reward is less than the one who caught (the full prayer). (T) 'And otherwise not': i.e., if he is not safe from losing the time, meaning there is tightness. (A) It was said: this applies to the sunnah of Asr and Isha, not Fajr and Dhuhr. I say: this needs elaboration: supererogatory prayers are of two types: confirmed sunnah (rawatib) and non-confirmed (what is additional). The worshipper either performs the obligatory prayer with congregation or alone. If with congregation, he definitely prays the rawatib sunan, and has no choice if possible. If alone, similarly in one narration; it is said he has a choice, and the first is more precautionary unless he fears losing time. As for non-rawatib, he has a choice absolutely. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning whether catching one rak'ah with the imam counts as praying with jama'ah. The matn states that catching one rak'ah does NOT make one a 'musalli bi jama'ah' for the purpose of an oath, but it does entitle one to the virtue (fadl) of congregational prayer. The commentary elaborates: a masbuq (one who joins late) who catches one rak'ah is not considered a full participant in the congregation; this is different from a lahiq (one who misses a rak'ah due to a valid excuse, who is legally behind the imam). The reward of the masbuq is less due to missing the first takbir. The rak'ah is not a minimum condition for the virtue; even catching the tashahhud secures some virtue of congregation by consensus. The commentary provides a practical example from al-Jami': if a man swears 'My slave is free if I pray Dhuhr with congregation' and he catches only one rak'ah, the oath is not broken because he is not considered praying 'with congregation' (since he was alone for part of the prayer). However, if he swore 'if I catch Dhuhr', then catching one rak'ah would break the oath, supported by the hadith 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Asr before sunset has caught Asr.' The commentary also discusses the second part of the matn about supererogatory prayers before the fard: if one prays with congregation, he definitely prays the rawatib sunan; if alone, he has a choice or should pray them. This applies to all rawatib, not just Dhuhr.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbuq): A latecomer who joins the prayer after the imam has started; here specifically one who catches only one rak'ah or less.
لاحق (lahiq): One who misses a part of the prayer due to a valid reason (e.g., sleep, forgetfulness) and is considered to be still following the imam legally.
فضل الجماعة (fadl al-jama'ah): The spiritual reward and virtue of praying in congregation, distinct from the legal ruling of praying with congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man swears 'My slave is free if I pray Dhuhr with congregation' and then he catches only one rak'ah behind the imam, does his oath break?
A) Yes, because he caught part of the prayer.
B) No, because he is not considered to have prayed the entire prayer with congregation.
C) It depends on whether he caught the first rak'ah.
D) Yes, because the hadith says whoever catches one rak'ah has caught the prayer.

Key Takeaway
Catching one rak'ah grants the virtue of congregation but does not constitute praying with the congregation for oath purposes; the rawatib sunan are prayed before the fard if time permits, but if time is tight, the fard takes priority.

Joining the Imam in Ruku and Bowing Before the Imam
Rulings on catching rak'ah and bowing before imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on catching a rak'ah by joining the imam in ruku and explain when bowing before the imam is valid but makruh tahrimi, and distinguish the Hanafi position from that of Zufar and al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
You must actually bow with the imam to catch the rak'ah; bowing before him is sinful but the prayer remains valid.

In congregational prayer, timing is crucial. This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses two common scenarios for the follower: when does joining the imam in ruku count as catching the rak'ah, and what if the follower bows before the imam? The rulings rely on the concept of participation (musharakah) and are supported by hadith. Let's analyze the Hanafi position and the disagreement with Zufar and al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues
The passage covers two distinct rulings: (1) whether a latecomer who catches the imam in ruku but does not bow immediately has caught the rak'ah; (2) whether a follower who bows before the imam has a valid prayer.
These are common practical scenarios in congregational prayer.
2
State the condition for catching a rak'ah
According to the Hanafi school, the condition for catching a rak'ah is actual participation (musharakah) in the action of ruku with the imam. If the follower bows with the imam, he catches the rak'ah; if he delays, he misses it.
The condition is derived from the need to follow the imam in actions.
3
Analyze the ruling on bowing before the imam
The text states that if a follower bows before the imam, his prayer is valid (sahih) but it is makruh tahrimi. The proof comes from hadith prohibiting racing the imam. The validity is based on eventual participation.
The hadith indicate prohibition but not nullification.
4
Examine the dispute with Zufar and al-Shafi'i
Zufar and al-Shafi'i argue that catching the imam in ruku without bowing is sufficient to catch the rak'ah, and that bowing before the imam invalidates the prayer unless repeated. The Hanafi school refutes both claims.
The practical difference: Hanafis require active participation; opponents consider presence enough.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The Hanafi position (as stated in the text with 'indana') is the relied-upon view. The prayer of one who bows before the imam is valid but sinful; a latecomer must bow with the imam to catch the rak'ah.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن أدرك إمامه راكعاً فكبر ووقف حتى رفع رأسه لم يدرك تلك الركعة، ولو ركع مقتد قبل الإمام صح.

لم يدرك تلك الركعة لأن الشرط هو المشاركة مع الإمام في أفعال الصلاة ولم توجد فيكون مسبوقاً فيقضيها بعد فراغه ولو وافقه في الركوع كان مدركا لها. (ط، ع)] وقال زفر والشافعي: يصير مدركاً لها؛ لأنه أدركه فيما له حكم القيام، فيصير هذا لاحقاً عندهما، فيأتي بها قبل فراغ الإمام، ولكن إن صلى بعد فراغه جاز، وعندنا: هو مسبوق بها حتى يأتي بها بعد فراغ الإمام، وعلى هذا الخلاف لو لم يقف حتى انحط للركوع، فرفع الإمام رأسه قبل أن يركع رمز الحقائق: ٨٥/١] وقال في "فتح المعين": ويجب عليه أن يتابع الإمام في السجدتين، وإن لم يحتسبا له كما لو اقتدى بالإمام بعد ما رفع رأسه من الركوع، ولو ترك المتابعة لا تفسد صلاته، وإنما قيد بقوله: "ووقف"؛ لأنه لو كبر ووافقه في الركوع فإنه يكون مدركاً لتلك الركعة اتفاقاً. ولو ركع مقتد إلخ: أي بعد ما قرأ ما تجزي قراءته، أما قبلها فلا يجزيه والركوع قبل الإمام مكروه؛ لقوله عليه: "لا تبادروني بالركوع والسجود"، وقوله عليه: "أما يخشى الذي يركع قبل الإمام أن يحول الله رأسه رأس حمار"، وهو يفيد كراهة التحريم للنهي وقال :زفر: لا يصح إذا لم يعد ؛ لأن ما أتى به قبل إمامه لا يعتد به، فكذا ما يبتنى عليه ولنا أن الشرط هو المشاركة في جزء، وقد وجدت. (فتح)
And if he catches his imam in ruku, so he says takbir and stands until he (the imam) raises his head, he has not caught that rak'ah. And if a follower bows before the imam, it is valid. He did not catch that rak'ah because the condition is participation with the imam in the actions of prayer, and it did not occur; thus he is a masbuq and makes it up after his (imam's) completion. If he joins him in ruku, he would be a catcher of it. (T, A) And Zufar and al-Shafi'i said: He becomes a catcher of it because he caught him in what has the ruling of standing; thus he becomes a lahiq according to them, and he performs it before the imam finishes. But if he prays after his completion, it is permissible. According to us, he is masbuq with respect to it until he performs it after the imam finishes. Upon this disagreement is if he did not stand but went down for ruku, and the imam raised his head before he bowed. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/85) And it is said in Fath al-Mu'in: He must follow the imam in the two prostrations, even if they are not counted for him, like if he followed the imam after he raised his head from ruku. If he abandons following, his prayer is not invalidated. He restricted it by his saying 'and stood' because if he said takbir and joined him in ruku, he would have caught that rak'ah by agreement. 'And if a follower bows etc.': i.e., after reciting what suffices for his recitation; as for before that, it is not sufficient. And bowing before the imam is disliked (makruh) due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Do not race me in ruku and sujud', and his statement: 'Does he who bows before the imam not fear that Allah will turn his head into a donkey's head?' This indicates prohibition (karahah tahrimiyah) because of the prohibition. And Zufar said: It is not valid if he does not repeat it because what he did before his imam is not considered; likewise what is built upon it. Our proof is that the condition is participation in a part, and it has been found. (Fath)
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding two issues: (1) catching a rak'ah by joining the imam in ruku, and (2) bowing before the imam. The matn states: if a person catches the imam in ruku (i.e., the imam is already bowing), and he says the takbir and stands (without immediately bowing) until the imam raises his head, then he has not caught that rak'ah. The commentary explains that the condition for catching the rak'ah is participation with the imam in the actions; if he delays bowing until after the imam rises, he missed the ruku. However, if he bows with the imam (i.e., joins him in ruku immediately), he catches the rak'ah by agreement. There is an ikhtilaf with Zufar and al-Shafi'i, who argue that catching the imam in ruku (even if one does not bow with him) suffices because being in ruku has the ruling of standing (qiyam) for the latecomer, making him a lahiq who can perform the missed rak'ah before the imam finishes. The Hanafi position is that he is masbuq and must make it up after the imam's salam. (2) The second ruling: if a follower bows before the imam (i.e., precedes him in ruku), the prayer is valid (sahih) but it is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) due to the hadith prohibiting racing the imam. Zufar says it is invalid if not repeated because the preceding action is not counted. The Hanafi proof is that participation in a part (e.g., joining the imam later in the same ruku) fulfills the condition of following.

Key Terms
مشاركة (musharakah): Participation of the follower with the imam in the same action (e.g., bowing) at the same time; a condition for being considered part of the congregation.
كراهة التحريم (karahah tahrimiyah): Prohibitive dislike: an action that is forbidden but not to the extent of being haram; doing it is sinful but the prayer is valid.
مسبوق (masbuq): A latecomer who misses part of the prayer and must make up missed rak'ahs after the imam's salam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a follower bows (i.e., goes into ruku) before the imam, what is the ruling on his prayer?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid but it is makruh tahrimi.
C) The prayer is invalid only if he does not repeat the ruku.
D) The prayer is valid and there is no dislike.

Key Takeaway
To catch a rak'ah with the imam, you must actually bow with him; bowing before him is sinful but the prayer remains valid.

Catching a Rak'ah with the Imam: Hanafi Position and Dispute
Ruling on catching a rak'ah in congregational prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on catching a rak'ah and explain why the opposing view of Zufar and al-Shafi'i is rejected in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
You must bow while the imam is in ruku to catch the rak'ah; standing and waiting does not count.

In congregational prayer, latecomers often wonder whether simply joining the imam mid-rak'ah is enough. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position: actual participation in the ruku is essential. We will also examine the differing view of Zufar and al-Shafi'i, who consider catching the imam in ruku sufficient. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to distinguish between conditions that involve active participation versus mere presence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling from the matn: the follower does not catch the rak'ah unless he bows while the imam is still in ruku.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Zufar (a Hanafi dissenter) and al-Shafi'i hold that catching the imam in ruku is enough to catch the rak'ah, even without bowing.
They argue ruku has the ruling of standing.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The opponent's dalil: the imam's ruku is considered a substitute for qiyam, so catching him in that state is like catching him in qiyam.
They consider the follower a 'lahiq' who can complete before the imam finishes.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: the condition is actual participation in the specific action (ruku), not a general state. The follower remains a masbuq and must make up the rak'ah after the imam's salam.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Hanafi follower must perform an extra rak'ah; Zufar/Shafi'i follower does not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب إدراك الفريضة
وإن أدرك إمامه راكعاً فكبر ووقف حتى رفع رأسه لم يدرك تلك الركعة، ولو ركع مقتد فأدرك إمامه فيه صح.
قبل الإمام
في هذا الركوع
لم يدرك تلك الركعة لأن الشرط هو المشاركة مع الإمام في أفعال الصلاة ولم توجد فيكون مسبوقاً فيقضيها بعد فراغه ولو وافقه في الركوع كان مدركا لها. (ط، ع)] وقال زفر والشافعي: يصير مدركاً لها؛ لأنه أدركه فيما له حكم القيام، فيصير هذا لاحقاً عندهما، فيأتي بها قبل فراغ الإمام، ولكن إن صلى بعد فراغه جاز، وعندنا: هو مسبوق بها حتى يأتي بها بعد فراغ الإمام، وعلى هذا الخلاف لو لم يقف حتى انحط للركوع، فرفع الإمام رأسه قبل أن يركع رمز الحقائق: ٨٥/١] وقال في "فتح المعين": ويجب عليه أن يتابع الإمام في السجدتين، وإن لم يحتسبا له كما لو اقتدى بالإمام بعد ما رفع رأسه من الركوع، ولو ترك المتابعة لا تفسد صلاته، وإنما قيد بقوله: "ووقف"؛ لأنه لو كبر ووافقه في الركوع فإنه يكون مدركاً لتلك الركعة اتفاقاً. ولو ركع مقتد إلخ: أي بعد ما قرأ ما تجزي قراءته، أما قبلها فلا يجزيه والركوع قبل الإمام مكروه؛ لقوله عليه: "لا تبادروني بالركوع والسجود"، وقوله عليه: "أما يخشى الذي يركع قبل الإمام أن يحول الله رأسه رأس حمار"، وهو يفيد كراهة التحريم للنهي وقال :زفر: لا يصح إذا لم يعد ؛ لأن ما أتى به قبل إمامه لا يعتد به، فكذا ما يبتنى عليه ولنا أن الشرط هو المشاركة في جزء، وقد وجدت. (فتح)
Chapter on Catching the Obligatory Prayer. If he catches his imam in ruku, and he says the takbir and stands until he (the imam) raises his head, he does not catch that rak'ah. But if the follower bows and catches his imam in it, it is valid. [Commentary:] ... He does not catch that rak'ah because the condition is participation with the imam in the actions of prayer, and it is not found, so he becomes a latecomer (masbuq) and makes it up after his (imam's) completion. And if he joins him in ruku, he catches it. Zufar and al-Shafi'i said: He catches it because he caught him in something that has the ruling of standing (qiyam), so he becomes a follower (lahiq) according to them, and he performs it before the imam finishes. But if he prays after his completion it is permissible. According to us, he is masbuq with respect to it until he performs it after the imam finishes. And upon this difference is the case if he did not stand until he (the imam) lowered for ruku, then the imam raised his head before he bowed. ... And it is said in Fath al-Mu'in: It is obligatory upon him to follow the imam in the two prostrations, even if they are not counted for him, just as if he followed the imam after he raised his head from ruku. And if he leaves the following, his prayer is not invalidated. He only restricted his statement 'and stood' because if he said the takbir and joined him in ruku, he catches that rak'ah by agreement. 'And if the follower bows' etc.: meaning after he reads what suffices for his recitation. As for before it, it does not suffice. And bowing before the imam is disliked (makruh) because of his statement, peace be upon him: 'Do not precede me in ruku and sujud' and his statement: 'Does the one who bows before the imam not fear that Allah may turn his head into a donkey's head?' This indicates prohibition (karahah tahrimiyyah) due to the prohibition. Zufar said: It is not valid if he does not repeat it, because what he did before his imam is not counted, and likewise what is built upon it. And our proof is that the condition is participation in a part, and it exists. (Fath)
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding catching a rak'ah when joining the imam in ruku. The matn states the Hanafi position: if you find the imam in ruku and you stand without bowing until the imam raises his head, you have missed that rak'ah; but if you bow and catch the imam in ruku, it is valid. The commentator explains that the condition for catching a rak'ah is to participate with the imam in the actions of the prayer. If you do not bow while the imam is still in ruku, you are considered a masbuq (latecomer) and must make up that rak'ah after the imam completes the prayer. The text then records the opposition of Zufar and al-Shafi'i, who argue that since the imam was still in a position that has the ruling of standing (i.e., ruku is a substitute for standing in terms of being caught), the follower catches the rak'ah and should perform the missed part before the imam finishes. The Hanafi response is that the follower is still a masbuq and must perform the rak'ah after the imam's salam. The passage also addresses the ruling on following the imam in prostrations even if they are not counted for the latecomer's original rak'ah, and the prohibition of bowing before the imam, which is considered makruh tahrimi based on prophetic prohibitions.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbuq): A latecomer who misses part of the prayer with the imam and must make it up after the imam's salam.
لاحق (lahiq): A follower who catches the imam in a position that has the ruling of standing, thus considered to have caught the rak'ah according to some scholars.
كراهة التحريم (karahah tahrimiyyah): A ruling of prohibition close to haram, based on a definitive prohibition (nahy) that is not absolutely certain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, when does a latecomer catch a rak'ah with the imam?
A) When he joins the imam at any point during the rak'ah.
B) When he says the takbir and bows while the imam is still in ruku.
C) When he stands until the imam raises his head from ruku.
D) When he catches the imam in sajdah.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, catching a rak'ah requires active participation in the ruku while the imam is still in that position; waiting without bowing means the rak'ah is missed.

The Obligation of Order (Tartib) Between Missed and Present Prayers
States the ruling that tartib is mustahaqq with evidence and refutation of Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that tartib is mustahaqq, identify its evidence, and explain why it is not fard, shart, or wajib.

Core Idea
Tartib is mustahaqq: obligatory in practice, not in belief.

In this passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, the author establishes the ruling on the order between missed prayers (fawa'it) and current prayers. He uses the term 'mustahaqq' to capture a precise level of obligation. We will trace the evidence, understand the terminology, and see how the Hanafi school defends this position against Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Understand the term 'mustahaqq'
Recognize why the author avoids 'fard', 'shart', or 'wajib'. Mustahaqq means obligatory in practice, not in belief, because the evidence is zanni and the obligation drops with forgetfulness.
Fard implies qat'i evidence; shart never drops; wajib omission does not nullify, but tartib omission nullifies the current prayer.
2
Identify the evidence for tartib
Examine the hadith of Ibn Umar (marfu') about praying with the imam then making up missed prayer and repeating, and the hadith of Jabir that the Prophet prayed Asr after sunset then Maghrib.
The athar of Ibn Umar is treated like a hadith; Sa'id ibn Abd al-Rahman narrated it as marfu' and was authenticated by Yahya ibn Ma'in.
3
Analyze the refutation of al-Shafi'i
Al-Shafi'i says tartib is sunna because each fard is independent. The Hanafi response uses analogy: Iman is independent yet a condition for all acts, and in jam' at 'Arafa, Zuhr is a condition for Asr.
The independence of an act does not preclude it from being a condition for another.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah)
According to Hanafis, if one prays a current prayer while remembering a missed one, the current prayer is invalid (if they remembered before starting and had no excuse). For Shafi'is, it is valid.
The difference is operational in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب قضاء الفوائت [ك ف] الترتيب بين الفائتة والوقتية وبين الفوائت مستحق، ويسقط. نوعان: وإنما فاتته من الصلاة الصلاة يجوز[؟] [ أي في بيان أحكام القضاء، وهو تسليم مثل الواجب بسببه. (ع)] اعلم أن المأمور به أداء: وهو تسليم عين الواجب وقضاء: وهو تسليم مثل الواجب من عنده فلهذا يقال: الديون تقضى بأمثالها، وقد تستعمل إحدى العبارتين في الأخرى، ولما فرغ من الأداء شرع في بيان أحكام القضاء وقال: "باب قضاء الفوائت"، ولم يقل: قضاء المتروكات ظناً بالمؤمنين خيراً؛ لأن ظاهر حال المسلم أنه لا يترك الصلاة قصداً، غير قصد لاشتغاله بأمر لابد منه كالقابلة إذا خافت موت الولد، والمسافر إذا خاف من اللصوص، ترى أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أخر الصلاة عن وقتها يوم الخندق، والدليل على وجوب القضاء قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: "إذا رقد أحدكم أو غفل عنها فليصلها إذا ذكرها"، فإن الله عز وجل يقول: ﴿وَأَقِمِ الصَّلاةَ لِذِكْرِي﴾ (طه:١٤)، وفيه إفادة كون القضاء عند الذكر فرضاً على الفور؛ لأن جزاء الشرط لا يتراخى عنه والقضاء فرض في الفرض وواجب في الواجب، وسنة في السنة يعني خصوص سنة الفجر إذا فاتت مع الفرض؛ لأن الصحيح عدم قضاء ما عداها وإن فاتت مع الفرض. (مسكين، فتح) مستحق [ أي واجب مفروض عملاً لا اعتقاداً حتى لا أداء الوقتية مع تذكر الفائتة، وكذا لا يجوز قضاء الفوائت بترك الترتيب بينهنّ. (ط)] وبه قال مالك وأحمد وجماعة من التابعين، ولم يقل: "فرض"؛ لانصراف المطلق إلى القطعي، ولا "شرط"؛ لأن الشرط حقيقة لا يسقط بالنسيان، وهذا يسقط به، ولا "واجب"؛ لأنه ما لا يفوت الجواز بفوته، وهذا يفوت به، فأتى بلفظ المستحق؛ ليمكن أن يتمشى على كل منها والمراد بالمستحق المفروض عملاً، وإنما كان الترتيب مستحقاً؛ لقول ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما: "من نسي صلاة فلم يذكرها إلا وهو مع الإمام فليصل الإمام، فإذا فرغ من صلاته فليصل التي نَسِيها، ثم يعد صلاته التي صلاها مع الإمام"، والأثر في مثله كالخبر، وقد رفعه سعيد بن عبد الرحمن، ووثقه يحيى بن معين وكذا حديث جابر رضي الله عنه أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم صلى العصر بعد ما غربت الشمس، ثم صلى المغرب بعدها يدلُّ على أن الترتيب مستحق؛ إذ لو كان مستحباً لما أخر المغرب التي يكره تأخيرها لأمر مستحب، وقال الشافعي: الترتيب سنة؛ لأن كل فرض أصل بنفسه، فلا يكون شرطاً لغيره، ولنا: أثر ابن عمر وجابر، وكونه أصلاً بنفسه لا ينافي أن يكون شرطاً لغيره كالإيمان أصل بنفسه، وليس بتبع للشيء، وهو شرط لصحة جميع العبادات، وأقرب منه أن تقديم الظهر شرط لصحة العصر في الجمع بعرفة فكذا ههنا. (فتح)
Chapter of Making up Missed Prayers: [Meaning: in explanation of the rulings of qada', which is delivering the like of the obligatory due to its cause. (A)] Know that what is commanded is ada': delivering the exact obligatory, and qada': delivering the like of the obligatory from oneself. Hence it is said: debts are repaid by their likes. Sometimes one expression is used for the other. When he finished from ada', he began to explain the rulings of qada' and said: 'Chapter of Making up Missed Prayers.' He did not say 'Chapter of Making up Neglected Prayers' out of good opinion of the believers, because the apparent state of a Muslim is that he does not leave prayer intentionally, but unintentionally due to being occupied with a necessary matter, like the midwife who fears for the child's life, or the traveler who fears thieves. Consider that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) delayed prayer from its time on the day of the trench. The evidence for the obligation of qada' is his saying: 'If one of you sleeps or forgets it, let him pray it when he remembers it.' For Allah the mighty and majestic says: 'And establish prayer for My remembrance' (Ta-Ha 20:14). In this is the indication that qada' upon remembering is an immediate obligation, because the consequence of a condition is not delayed from it. Qada' is fard in fard, wajib in wajib, and sunna in sunna, meaning specifically the sunna of Fajr if missed along with the fard, because the correct view is that no other sunna is made up even if missed with the fard. (Miskin, Fath) 'Mustahaqq' [meaning: an obligation in practice, not in belief, such that performing the current prayer while remembering a missed one is not permissible, and similarly making up missed prayers without order between them is not permissible. (T)] This is also the view of Malik, Ahmad, and a group of the Tabi'un. He did not say 'fard' because the absolute term turns to the definitive; nor 'shart' because the condition in reality is not dropped by forgetfulness, while this drops by it; nor 'wajib' because that whose omission does not nullify permissibility is not wajib, while this nullifies it. So he used the term 'mustahaqq' so that it can suit each of these. The meaning of mustahaqq is that which is ordained in practice. The order was only mustahaqq due to the statement of Ibn Umar: 'Whoever forgets a prayer and only remembers while with the imam, let him pray with the imam, and when he finishes his prayer, let him pray the one he forgot, then repeat his prayer that he prayed with the imam.' An athar in such matters is like a khabar. Sa'id ibn Abd al-Rahman narrated it as marfu', and Yahya ibn Ma'in authenticated him. Similarly, the hadith of Jabir that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed Asr after the sun had set, then prayed Maghrib after it, indicates that order is mustahaqq; for if it were recommended, he would not have delayed Maghrib, whose delay is disliked, for a recommended matter. Al-Shafi'i said: 'Order is sunna, because each fard is an independent act, so it cannot be a condition for another.' Our evidence: the athar of Ibn Umar and Jabir, and its being independent does not negate being a condition for another, like Iman is independent and yet is a condition for the validity of all acts of worship. And closer than this is that the performance of Zuhr is a condition for the validity of Asr in the jam' at 'Arafa, so here too. (Fath)
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary (sharh) establishes the ruling that the order (tartib) between missed prayers (fawa'it) and current prayers (waqtiyya) is mustahaqq—obligatory in practice (wajib amalan). The author explains why he uses 'mustahaqq' rather than 'fard' (because fard implies definitive evidence, whereas the proofs here are ahad), 'shart' (because a condition is never dropped by forgetfulness, but this obligation is dropped in certain cases), or 'wajib' (because omission here nullifies permissibility, unlike regular wajib). The evidence includes: (1) the hadith of Ibn Umar that one who forgets a prayer and remembers while with the imam should pray with him, then make up the missed prayer, then repeat the congregational prayer; (2) the hadith of Jabir that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed Asr after sunset and then Maghrib, showing that order was maintained even though Maghrib is normally performed before sunset. The passage then refutes Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that tartib is only sunna because each prayer is independent. The Hanafi response is that independence does not preclude being a condition for another act, as Iman is independent yet a condition for all acts, and in the jam' at 'Arafa, Zuhr is a condition for 'Asr. Thus, the Hanafi position is that tartib is obligatory (mustahaqq).

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'): Delivering the like of the obligatory act after its time has passed.
أداء (ada'): Delivering the exact obligatory act in its appointed time.
ترتيب (tartib): The obligation to pray missed prayers in chronological order before present prayers.
مستحق (mustahaqq): Something that is obligatory in practice (amalan), not necessarily in belief (i'tiqadan). It indicates a level of obligation between fard and wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school use the term 'mustahaqq' for tartib rather than 'fard' or 'shart'?
A) Because the evidence is qat'i.
B) Because the obligation drops in cases of forgetfulness, unlike a condition (shart).
C) Because it is sunna, not obligatory.
D) Because it is a condition that never drops.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that order between missed and present prayers is mustahaqq (obligatory in practice), supported by hadith and qiyas, and its deliberate omission invalidates the current prayer.

Three Causes for Dropping the Obligation of Order Between Prayers
Explains three conditions dropping order obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions under which the order (tartib) between missed and current prayers drops, and apply the Hanafi ruling to scenarios involving narrow time, forgetfulness, or abundance of missed prayers.

Core Idea
The obligation of order drops due to narrow time, forgetfulness, or abundance (six or more missed prayers).

The Hanafi school requires that missed prayers be made up in order before the current prayer, but exceptions exist for practical necessity. This lesson explores the three causes that lift the order requirement, the prophetic proof, and the key disagreements within the school and with other imams. Understanding these exceptions prevents unnecessary invalidation of prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three causes
List the three excuses (dhiq al-waqt, nisyan, kathrat al-fawa'it) and the effect on the order. Note that each cause independently drops the obligation.
The order drops only when the cause is present; otherwise it remains wajib.
2
Analyze the proof for forgetfulness
Examine the hadith of the Prophet (ﷺ) who prayed Maghrib, then asked about Asr, and prayed Asr without repeating Maghrib. This indicates that forgetfulness drops the order.
The hadith is a khabar wahid but deemed sufficient for this ruling.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi disputes on abundance
Compare the views of Abu Hanifa (six), Zufar (one month), and Muhammad (five) on what constitutes kathrat. Understand why Zahir al-Riwayah's 'six' is preferred.
Remember: the sixth prayer must exit its time for the order to drop.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i position
State that Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the current prayer is not invalidated if one remembers a missed prayer while performing it. Contrast with the Hanafi view that it becomes fasid.
The thamarah al-khilaf is whether the current prayer must be repeated.

Source Text

ويسقط إلخ: أي الترتيب بين قضاء الفوائت وأداء الوقتية يسقط بأحدى خصال ثلاث: الأول ضيق الوقت بأن تذكر في آخر الوقت بحيث لو اشتغل بالفائتة يخرج الوقت قبل أداء الوقتية، فيسقط الترتيب؛ لأن في مراعاته إبطال العمل بالدليل المقطوع به، وهو أداء الصلاة في وقتها، والثاني النسيان؛ لما ذكرنا أن خبر الواحد جعل بضيق الوقت، والنسيان وصيرورتها ستا، ولم يعد بعودها إلى القلة، فلو صلى فرضا الفائتة س م ز ذاكرا فائتة ولو وترا فسد فرضه موقوفا. كانت أي الترتيب أي الفوائت كفجر مثلا وقت تذكره وقتا للفائتة، ولا تذكرها هنا، فوجب العمل بالدليل المقطوع به، وروي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام صلى المغرب يوما، فقال هل رآني أحد منكم صليت العصر، فقالوا: لا، فصلى العصر ولم يعد المغرب، ولو وجب الترتيب مع النسيان لأعاد المغرب، والثالث كثرة الفوائت ثم اختلفوا في أدنى حد الكثرة، ففي ظاهر الرواية أن يصير الفوائت ستا، فإذا خرج وقت السادسة سقط الترتيب، وعند زفر أن يزيد على شهر كالجنون إذا استغرق الشهر، وروي عن محمد أن السقوط بصيرورتها خمسا والصحيح جواب ظاهر الرواية؛ لأن الفائتة لا تدخل في حد التكرار بدخول وقت السادسة وإنما تدخل بخروج وقت السادس (مستخلص) وقال ملا مسكين: سواء كانت الفائتة قديمة أو حديثة، فالحديثة تسقط الترتيب اتفاقا، وفي القديمة اختلاف المشايخ، وذلك كمن ترك صلاة شهر، ثم صلى مدة ولم يقض تلك الصلوات حتى ترك صلاة، ثم صلى أخرى ذاكرا للفائتة الحديثة لم تجز عند البعض، ويجعل الماضي كأن لم يكن زجرا له، وقيل تجوز، وعليه الفتوى؛ لأن الاشتغال بهذه الفائتة ليس بأولى من الاشتغال بالفوائت القديمة، وفي الاشتغال بالكل تفويت الفريضة عن وقتها. (انتهى مع زيادة من الفتح) بضيق الوقت لأنه ليس من الحكمة تفويت الوقتية، والمراد من الوقت المستحب في الأصح. (ط،ع) والنسيان للفائتة؛ لأن الناسي عاجز حتى لو نسي الفائتة وصلى الوقتية ثم تذكرها، يقضي الفائتة ولم يعد الوقتية، وقال مالك: لا يسقط بهما. (مسكين) وصيرورتها: أي يسقط أيضا مع صيرورة الفائتة ست صلوات بخروج وقت السادسة. (مسكين) إلى القلة بأن كانت عليه صلوات فائتة، فقضى بعضها حتى قل ما بقي لا يعود الترتيب فيما بقي؛ لأن الساقط لا يحتمل العود، وقال أبو حفص الكبير وعليه الفتوى، وهو اختيار شمس الأئمة وفخر الإسلام، وقيل: يعود الترتيب. (ع) موقوفا [ أي فسادا موقوفا عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما تفسد فسادا باتا] أي لو صلى العصر مثلا ذاكرا أنه لم يصل الظهر فسد عصره إن لم يكن في آخر الوقت والعبرة لأصل الوقت عندهما، وعند محمد للوقت المستحب حتى لو شرع في العصر وهو ناس للظهر، ثم تذكر الظهر في وقت لو اشتغل به يقع العصر في الوقت المكروه، يقطع العصر عندهما ويصلي الظهر ثم يصلي العصر، وعنده يمضي في العصر ثم يصلي الظهر بعد غروب الشمس، فإذا فسدت الفريضة لا يبطل أصل الصلاة عندهما، وعند محمد يبطل، كذا ذكر عامة مشايخنا هذا الاختلاف، وقيل: لا خلاف بينهم بأنه لا يبطل أصل الصلاة، ثم العصر يفسد فسادا موقوفا حتى لو صلى بعده ست صلوات أو أكثر ولم يعد الظهر أعاد الكل جائزا، وعندهما يفسد فسادا باتا لا جواز له بحال، وقال الشافعي: لا يفسد أصلا، وقوله: "ولو وترا" أي ولو كان المتروك وترا فكذلك عنده خلافا لهما. (مسكين)
'and it drops' etc.: Meaning that the order between making up missed prayers and performing the current prayer drops by one of three characteristics: First, narrowness of time: that one remembers at the end of the time such that if he occupies himself with the missed prayer, the time for the current prayer would exit before performing it. So the order drops because maintaining it would mean nullifying the established evidence, which is performing prayer in its time. Second, forgetfulness: because what we mentioned that the khabar wahid made it due to narrowness of time and forgetfulness and its becoming six, and it does not return by it returning to fewness. So if one prays a fard while remembering a missed prayer, even if witr, his fard becomes suspendedly invalid. The order [meaning of the missed prayers] was like Fajr, for example, the time of his remembering was a time for the missed prayer, and he did not remember it then, so it is necessary to act on the established evidence. And it is narrated that he (peace be upon him) one day prayed Maghrib and said: 'Has anyone of you seen me pray Asr?' They said: No. So he prayed Asr and did not repeat Maghrib. If order were obligatory with forgetfulness, he would have repeated Maghrib. Third, abundance of missed prayers. Then they differed on the minimum of abundance. In Zahir al-Riwayah, it is that the missed prayers become six. So when the time of the sixth exits, the order drops. According to Zufar, it must exceed a month, like madness if it covers a month. It is narrated from Muhammad that it drops by becoming five. The correct is the answer of Zahir al-Riwayah, because the missed prayer does not enter the limit of repetition by entering the time of the sixth but only by exiting the time of the sixth. (Mustakhlas) Mulla Miskin said: Whether the missed prayer is old or new, the new one drops the order by agreement. In the old one, there is difference among the mashayikh. For example, one who missed a month of prayers, then prayed for a period without making up those prayers until he missed another prayer, then prayed another while remembering the new missed one. It is not valid according to some, and the past is made as if it were not as a deterrent. It is said it is valid, and on this is the fatwa, because occupying with this missed prayer is not more preferable than occupying with the old missed prayers, and occupying with all would cause the loss of the fard from its time. (End with addition from Fath) Due to narrowness of time, because it is not wise to lose the current prayer. And the intended is the preferred time according to the more correct view. (T, A) And forgetfulness of the missed prayer, because the forgetful one is incapable. So if one forgets the missed prayer and prays the current prayer, then remembers, he makes up the missed prayer and does not repeat the current prayer. Malik said: It does not drop by either. (Miskin) 'And its becoming six': meaning it also drops with the missed prayers becoming six prayers upon exiting the time of the sixth. (Miskin) 'To fewness': If one has missed prayers and makes up some until what remains becomes few, the order does not return in what remains because what is dropped cannot return. Abu Hafs al-Kabir said this, and on it is the fatwa, and it is the choice of Shams al-A'imma and Fakhr al-Islam. It was said: The order returns. (A) 'Mawqufan' [meaning invalidity suspended according to Abu Hanifa, and according to them it invalidates absolutely] i.e., if one prays Asr, for example, while remembering that he did not pray Zuhr, his Asr is invalid if he is not at the end of the time. The consideration is of the original time according to them. According to Muhammad, it is of the preferred time. So if he begins Asr while forgetful of Zuhr, then remembers Zuhr at a time when if he occupied with it, Asr would fall in the disliked time, according to them he breaks Asr and prays Zuhr then Asr. According to him, he continues in Asr then prays Zuhr after sunset. So when the fard becomes invalid, the original prayer does not invalidate according to them, but according to Muhammad it invalidates. Thus most of our scholars mentioned this difference. It was said: There is no difference between them that it does not invalidate the original prayer. Then Asr is invalid with suspended invalidity, so if he prays after it six or more prayers and does not repeat Zuhr, he redoes all as valid. According to them, it invalidates absolutely and can never be valid. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not invalid at all. His saying: 'even if witr' means even if the missed one was witr, so likewise according to him contrary to them. (Miskin)
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage details the three conditions under which the obligation of order (tartib) between missed and current prayers drops. The first is narrowness of time (dhiq al-waqt): if one remembers a missed prayer near the end of the current prayer's time such that he cannot pray both on time, he should pray the current prayer first. The second is forgetfulness (nisyan): if one forgets the missed prayer and prays the current one, the order drops. Evidence is the incident where the Prophet prayed Maghrib, then remembered he had not prayed Asr, so he prayed Asr without repeating Maghrib. The third is abundance of missed prayers (kathrat al-fawa'it). The minimum for abundance is a point of intra-Hanafi dispute: Zahir al-Riwayah holds it is six prayers (i.e., when the sixth prayer's time exits), Zufar says a month, and Muhammad says five. The relied-upon view is six, because only after that does the missed prayer enter the category of repetition. Once the order drops, it does not return even if the number of missed prayers reduces. The passage also discusses the effect of forgetting: Abu Hanifa holds that if one prays a current prayer while remembering a missed one, the current prayer is invalid with suspended invalidity (fasid mawquf)—it may become valid if later circumstances change. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that it is absolutely invalid (fasid battan). There is also a dispute about whether the original prayer (the missed one) is invalidated; the preferred view is that it is not. Malik holds that forgetfulness does not drop the order at all. The commentary highlights that the fatwa is on the view that the order drops for new missed prayers but not for old ones, and that the current prayer invalidates only if one remembers while praying; if he forgets, it is valid.

Key Terms
ضيق الوقت (dhiq al-waqt): Narrowness of the prayer time such that performing a missed prayer would cause the current prayer to miss its time.
كثرة الفوائت (kathrat al-fawa'it): The condition of having many missed prayers; the minimum in the Hanafi school is six prayers (Zahir al-Riwayah).
فساد موقوف (fasid mawquf): An invalidity that is suspended; the act is invalid but may become valid later if conditions change (e.g., if one prays enough subsequent prayers).
وتر (witr): The witr prayer, which is considered a fard according to Abu Hanifa (wajib) and is included in the ruling of tartib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Zahir al-Riwayah, what is the minimum number of missed prayers that constitutes 'abundance' (kathrat) causing the order to drop?
A) Five
B) Six
C) One month's worth
D) Three

Key Takeaway
The obligation of order between missed and current prayers drops due to narrow time, forgetfulness, or six or more missed prayers, and once dropped it does not return.

Conditions for Dropping the Obligation of Order in Qada'
Rulings on when order of missed prayers becomes non-obligatory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions that lift the obligation of order (tartib) in making up missed prayers and apply them to given scenarios.

Core Idea
The obligation of order in qada' drops due to narrow time, forgetfulness, or six missed prayers.

The Hanafi school holds that making up missed prayers in order (tartib) is wajib. However, this obligation is not absolute; it drops under specific circumstances. This lesson covers the three conditions that lift the requirement of tartib, supported by a hadith and the rulings of the early Hanafi masters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that tartib (order) in making up missed prayers is initially wajib. This comes from the general obligation to perform missed prayers as soon as possible.
The ruling is not fard because the evidence is from a hadith (zanni).
2
List the three conditions that drop tartib
The text mentions: (1) narrowness of time for the current prayer, (2) forgetfulness of the missed prayer, and (3) the missed prayers becoming numerous (six or more).
Each condition has its own rationale; forgetfulness is excused because the forgetful person is considered incapacitated.
3
Locate the dalil for forgetfulness dropping tartib
The hadith of the Prophet (saw) praying Asr after Maghrib without repeating Maghrib when he forgot is cited as proof that forgetfulness lifts the obligation of order.
The text states 'the definitive proof' (al-dalil al-maqtu' bih).
4
Analyze the dispute on the minimum number for numerousness
The apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwaya) sets six missed prayers as the threshold. Zufar says it is a month; Muhammad (in one narration) says five. The correct position is six because a missed prayer enters the count only after its time exits.
The fatwa is upon the view that once tartib drops, it does not return (Abu Hafs al-Kabir).

باب قضاء الفوائت بضيق الوقت، والنسيان وصيرُورتها ستَّا، ولم يعد بعودها إلى القلة، فلو صلى فرضاً ذاكراً فائتة ولو وتراً فشد فرضه موقوفا. كانت أي الترتيب أي الفوائت كفجر مثلاً وقت تذكره وقتاً للفائتة، ولا تذكرها هنا، فوجب العمل بالدليل المقطوع به، وروي أنه عليه صلى المغرب يوماً، فقال هل رآني أحد منكم صليت العصر، فقالوا: لا، فصلى العصر ولم يعد المغرب، ولو وجب الترتيب مع النسيان لأعاد المغرب، والثالث كثرة الفوائت ثم اختلفوا في أدنى حد الكثرة، ففي ظاهر الرواية أن يصير الفوائت ستا، فإذا خرج وقت السادسة سقط الترتيب، وعند زفر أن يزيد على شهر كالجنون إذا استغرق الشهر، وروي عن محمد أن السقوط بصيرورتها خمسا والصحيح جواب ظاهر الرواية؛ لأن الفائتة لا تدخل في حد التكرار بدخول وقت السادسة وإنما تدخل بخروج وقت السادس (مستخلص) وقال ملا مسكين: سواء كانت الفائتة قديمة أو حديثة، فالحديثة تسقط الترتيب اتفاقا، وفي القديمة اختلاف المشايخ، وذلك كمن ترك صلاة شهر، ثم صلّى مدة ولم يقض تلك الصلوات حتى ترك صلاة، ثم صلى أخرى ذاكراً للفائتة الحديثة لم تجز عند البعض، ويجعل الماضي كأن لم يكن زجراً له، وقيل تجوز، وعليه الفتوى؛ لأن الاشتغال بهذه الفائتة ليس بأولى من الاشتغال بالفوائت القديمة، وفي الاشتغال بالكل تفويت الفريضة عن وقتها. (انتهى مع زيادة من الفتح) بضيق الوقت لأنه ليس من الحكمة تفويت الوقتية، والمراد من الوقت المستحب في الأصح. (ط،ع) والنسيان للفائتة؛ لأن الناسي عاجز حتى لو نسي الفائتة وصلى الوقتية ثم تذكرها، يقضي الفائتة ولم يعد الوقتية، وقال مالك: لا يسقط بهما. (مسكين) وصيرورتها: أي يسقط أيضاً مع صيرورة الفائتة ست صلوات بخروج وقت السادسة. (مسكين) إلى القلة بأن كانت عليه صلوات فائتة، فقضى بعضها حتى قل ما بقي لا يعود الترتيب فيما بقي؛ لأن الساقط لا يحتمل العود، وقال أبو حفص الكبير وعليه الفتوى، وهو اختيار شمس الأئمة وفخر الإسلام، وقيل: يعود الترتيب. (ع) موقوفاً [ أي فساداً موقوفاً عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما تفسد فساداً باتاً] أي لو صلى العصر مثلاً ذاكراً أنه لم يصل الظهر فسد عصره إن لم يكن في آخر الوقت والعبرة لأصل الوقت عندهما، وعند محمد للوقت المستحب حتى لو شرع في العصر وهو ناس للظهر ، ثم تذكر الظهر في وقت لو اشتغل به يقع العصر في الوقت المكروه، يقطع العصر عندهما ويصلي الظهر ثم يصلي العصر، وعنده يمضي في العصر ثم يصلي الظهر بعد غروب الشمس، فإذا فسدت الفريضة لا يبطل أصل الصلاة عندهما، وعند محمد يبطل، كذا ذكر عامة مشايخنا هذا الاختلاف، وقيل: لا خلاف بينهم بأنه لا يبطل أصل الصلاة، ثم العصر يفسد فسادا موقوفاً حتى لو صلى بعده ست صلوات أو أكثر و لم يعد الظهر أعاد الكل جائزاً، وعندهما يفسد فسادا باتاً لا جواز له بحال، وقال الشافعي: لا يفسد أصلاً، وقوله: "ولو وتراً" أي ولو كان المتروك وتراً فكذلك عنده خلافاً لهما. (مسكين)
Chapter on Making Up Missed Prayers: [The obligation of order] drops due to narrowness of time, forgetfulness, and their becoming six, and it does not return when they become few. So if one prays a current obligation while remembering a missed prayer, even if it is Witr, then his current prayer becomes suspended invalid [according to Abu Hanifa]. [Commentary] meaning the order of the missed prayers. For example, if one remembers a missed Fajr during the time of [another] prayer, that time becomes a time for the missed prayer, and he does not perform it here? So it is obligatory to act on the definitive proof. It is narrated that he (peace be upon him) prayed Maghrib one day and said, 'Did any of you see me pray Asr?' They said, 'No.' So he prayed Asr and did not repeat Maghrib. If order were obligatory despite forgetfulness, he would have repeated Maghrib. The third [condition] is numerousness of missed prayers. Then they differed on the minimum of numerousness: in the apparent narration, it is that the missed prayers become six; when the time of the sixth exits, order drops. According to Zufar, it exceeds a month, like insanity if it covers a month. It is narrated from Muhammad that the dropping occurs when they become five, and the correct is the answer of the apparent narration because a missed prayer does not enter into the limit of repetition with the entering of the time of the sixth but enters with the exiting of the time of the sixth. (Mustakhlas) Mulla Miskin said: Whether the missed prayer is old or new, the new one drops the order by agreement. Regarding the old one, there is disagreement among the mashayikh. For example, if one leaves a month of prayers, then prays for a while without making up those prayers until he leaves a prayer, then prays another remembering the new missed prayer, it is not valid according to some, and they make the past as if it never happened as a deterrent. It is said it is valid, and that is the fatwa because occupying oneself with this missed prayer is not more deserving than occupying oneself with old missed prayers, and occupying oneself with all would cause the loss of the obligatory prayer in its time. (End with addition from al-Fath) [The dropping] is due to narrowness of time because it is not from wisdom to lose the timely prayer, and what is meant is the recommended time according to the most correct. (T, A) And forgetfulness of the missed prayer because the forgetful person is incapacitated. So if one forgets the missed prayer and prays the timely prayer, then remembers it, he makes up the missed prayer and does not repeat the timely prayer. Malik said: It does not drop by these two. (Miskin) And their becoming six: i.e., it drops also with the missed prayers becoming six prayers by the exit of the time of the sixth. (Miskin) To fewness: if one has missed prayers, so he makes up some until what remains is few, the order does not return regarding what remains because that which has dropped does not bear returning. Abu Hafs al-Kabir said, and the fatwa is upon it, and it is the choice of Shams al-A'imma and Fakhr al-Islam. It is said the order returns. (A) Suspended: i.e., suspended invalidity according to Abu Hanifa, and according to the two, it becomes absolutely invalid. i.e., if one prays Asr for example while remembering that he did not pray Zuhr, then his Asr becomes invalid if it is not at the end of the time, and the consideration is for the beginning of time according to the two, and according to Muhammad it is for the recommended time. So if one begins Asr while forgetful of Zuhr, then remembers Zuhr at a time that if he occupied himself with it, Asr would fall in the disliked time, then he cuts off Asr according to the two and prays Zuhr then Asr. According to him, he continues in Asr then prays Zuhr after sunset. So when the obligatory prayer becomes invalid, the origin of the prayer is not nullified according to the two, but according to Muhammad it is nullified. Thus most of our mashayikh mentioned this disagreement. It is said there is no disagreement among them that the origin of the prayer is not nullified. Then Asr becomes invalid with suspended invalidity so that if he prays after it six prayers or more and does not repeat Zuhr, he repeats all validly. According to the two, it becomes absolutely invalid with no validity at all. Al-Shafi'i said: It does not become invalid at all. And his saying: 'even if it is Witr' means even if the missed is Witr, likewise according to him, contrary to the two. (Miskin)

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on making up missed prayers (Qada' al-Fawa'it) presents the rulings on when the obligation to perform missed prayers in order (tartib) drops. The author begins by stating three conditions that lift the requirement of tartib: (1) narrowness of time for the current prayer, meaning if one fears losing the current prayer's recommended time, he may pray it before making up the missed one; (2) forgetfulness of the missed prayer—the forgetful person is excused and does not need to repeat the current prayer upon remembering; and (3) the missed prayers becoming numerous, defined in the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwaya) as six missed prayers. Once the time of the sixth missed prayer exits, tartib drops. The text then discusses disagreements: Zufar defines numerousness as exceeding a month, while a narration from Muhammad suggests five. The correct position is the apparent narration because a missed prayer does not enter the count of repetition until its time exits. The passage then addresses a scenario where a person remembers a missed prayer while performing a current prayer. According to Abu Hanifa, the current prayer becomes 'suspended invalid' (fasad mawquf)—it is invalid but can be rendered valid if the missed prayer is later made up before six more prayers pass. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani), it becomes absolutely invalid (fasad ba't) and cannot be redeemed. The text also notes that al-Shafi'i holds it does not become invalid at all. The relied-upon fatwa is on the view of Abu Hafs al-Kabir that once tartib drops due to numerousness, it does not return even if the missed prayers become few. This chapter is a key source for understanding Hanafi rulings on making up missed prayers and the intricacies of order.

Key Terms
الترتيب (al-tartib): The order in which missed prayers are made up, starting from the earliest missed, unless conditions for dropping apply.
الفائتة (al-fa'itah): A prayer that was missed and must be made up.
فساد موقوف (fasad mawquf): Suspended invalidity: the prayer is invalid but may become valid if conditions are later fulfilled (e.g., missed prayer made up before six more prayers pass).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwaya), when does the obligation of order in making up missed prayers drop due to numerousness?
A) When the missed prayers become more than five.
B) When the missed prayers become six, and the time of the sixth exits.
C) When the missed prayers are all for fard prayers.
D) When the missed prayers are from a month of neglect.

Key Takeaway
The obligation of order in qada' drops when missed prayers reach six (by exit of the sixth's time), and once dropped, it does not return.
